Al-Baqillani's Hidden Piety and Outward Severity
Biographical report on al-Baqillani's character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani's outward harshness was a deliberate strategy to protect the honor of Islamic scholarship, while his inner piety was even greater.

Core Idea
Outward severity can be a shield for inner piety.

This passage gives us a rare glimpse into the personal character of Imam al-Baqillani. We learn that his public persona of strictness was intentional, designed to deter enemies of Islam from disrespecting scholars. At the same time, he concealed a far deeper level of piety. Let's examine the report and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the full meaning.
Notice the contrast between what he concealed (أضمر) and what he manifested (أظهر).
2
Understand the contrast between hidden and manifest piety
The report states that his hidden piety was many times greater than what he showed. Identify the virtues mentioned: الورع, الديانة, الزهد, الصيانة.
3
Analyze al-Baqillani's stated reason for outward anger
Focus on his answer: he manifests anger to prevent enemies from belittling the scholars of truth. List the groups he names.
This shows his outward severity was a protective measure, not a reflection of his inner state.
4
Reflect on the prophetic allusion
The final sentence alludes to prophets (Adam, David, Joseph, Muhammad) who had inner tests or states. Consider what this implies about al-Baqillani's own hidden piety.
The text is somewhat obscure; scholars interpret it as comparing his concealment to the prophets' inner experiences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حفظه من وعن الشيخ الإمام أبو حاتم محمود بن الحسين القزويني أن ما كان يضمره القاضي الإمام أبو بكر الأشعري رضي الله عنه من الورع والديانة والزهد والصيانة أضعاف ما كان يظهره فقيل له في ذلك فقال : إنما أظهر ما أظهره غيظاً لليهود والنصارى والمعتزلة والرافضة والمخالفين لئلا يستحقروا علماء الحق والدين فأضمر ما أضمره فإني رأيت أكرم مع جلالته نودي عليه بذوقه وداود بنظره ويوسف بهمه ومحمد بخطرة عليهم السلام .
His memory: And from al-Shaykh al-Imam Abu Hatim Mahmud ibn al-Husayn al-Qazwini: That what al-Qadi al-Imam Abu Bakr al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, concealed of piety, religiosity, asceticism, and integrity was many times more than what he manifested. So he was asked about that, and he said: I only manifest what I manifest out of anger against the Jews, Christians, Mu'tazila, Rawafid, and opponents, lest they belittle the scholars of truth and religion. And I conceal what I conceal, for I saw the Most Generous with His majesty, called upon with his eating? and David with his glance, and Joseph with his passion, and Muhammad with his thought, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage reveals the inner piety of Imam al-Baqillani. Al-Qazwini reports that his hidden virtues—piety, religiosity, asceticism, integrity—were many times greater than what he showed outwardly. When questioned, the Imam explained that his outward severity was a deliberate display of anger against enemies of Islam (Jews, Christians, Mu'tazila, Rawafid) to prevent them from belittling the scholars of truth. He then alludes to prophets who were tested or called upon in specific ways, suggesting that his hidden piety was even greater, similar to how prophets had inner dimensions.

Key Terms
الورع
الديانة
الزهد
الصيانة
الغيظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that al-Baqillani's outward harshness reflected his true personality or that he was an angry person.
Correction: The passage clarifies that his outward anger was a strategic display to protect the honor of scholars, while his inner state was one of immense piety and gentleness.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Baqillani say he manifested outward anger?
A) Because he was naturally angry
B) To protect the scholars of truth from being belittled by enemies
C) To scare his students into learning
D) Because he disliked the people of Baghdad

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani's outward harshness was a calculated defense of truth, while his hidden piety was far greater.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How much of your outward piety is genuine, and how much is performed for the approval of others? What would it cost you to be as inwardly devout as al-Baqillani while appearing harsh to those who oppose the truth?
?
When you feel anger at those who distort the religion, is it truly for Allah's sake or is it tainted by pride? How can you purify your motives so that your severity, if needed, is a shield for the truth and not a weapon for your ego?
?
You hide your faults and display your virtues—but what if your inner state is many times weaker than your outer show? Would you be willing to be seen as less pious than you are, as al-Baqillani was seen as harsher, for a higher purpose? What step will you take today to align your inner and outer self?

Al-Baqillani's Victory in Debate Against Ibn Mujahid
Account of an all-night debate won by al-Baqillani in Baghdad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the recognition al-Baqillani received from scholars of other madhhabs due to his mastery in debate.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani's victory in debate earned him the endorsement of a Hanbali imam.

This passage recounts a famous debate between Imam al-Baqillani and the Shafi'i scholar Ibn Mujahid in Baghdad. The all-night discussion on ijtihad ended with al-Baqillani's argument prevailing, leading the Hanbali scholar al-Tamimi to urge his followers to hold fast to him. It illustrates al-Baqillani's high standing among contemporaneous scholars.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setting
Al-Baqillani arrives in Baghdad and is invited by the Hanbali scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi. Note that al-Tamimi is described as the imam of his time in his madhhab, setting the stage for the debate.
2
Identify the participants
Besides al-Tamimi, the attendees include Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Mujahid (the opponent), Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un, and Abu al-Hasan al-Faqih. Recognize the caliber of scholars present.
Ibn Mujahid is a well-known Shafi'i scholar.
3
Follow the debate
The issue of ijtihad is debated between al-Baqillani and Ibn Mujahid. The discussion continues until dawn, showing its depth and intensity.
The lengthy debate indicates both scholars' thoroughness.
4
Note the outcome
The text states that 'the argument of al-Qadi prevailed over him' (ظهر كلام القاضي عليه). Al-Baqillani emerges victorious in the debate.
5
Reflect on the aftermath
After the debate, al-Tamimi tells his companions to hold fast to al-Baqillani, saying the Sunnah will never be free of need of him. This highlights the respect al-Baqillani commanded.
This endorsement from a Hanbali leader is significant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن عبد الله الحسين بن محمد الدامغاني قال : لما قدم القاضي الإمام أبو بكر الباقلاني بغداد دعاه الشيخ أبو الحسن التميمي الحنبلي رحمهما الله بن إمام عصره في مذهبه وشيخ مصره في رهطة وحضر الشيخ أبو عبد الله مجاهد والشيخ أبو الحسين محمد بن أحمد بن سمعون وأبو الحسن الفقيه فجرت مسئلة الاجتهاد بين القاضي أبي بكر وبين أبي عبد الله بن مجاهد وتعلق الكلام بينهما إلى أن انفجر عمود الصبح وظهر كلام القاضي عليه رحمهما الله وكان أبو الحسن التميمي الحنبلي يقول لأصحابه تمسكوا بهذا الرجل فليس للسنة عنه غنى أبداً (١).
And from 'Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Damghani, he said: When al-Qadi al-Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani came to Baghdad, al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi al-Hanbali, may Allah have mercy on them, invited him, (he being) the imam of his time in his madhhab and the shaykh of his city in his group? and attended al-Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Mujahid, and al-Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Sam'un, and Abu al-Hasan al-Faqih. Then the issue of ijtihad arose between al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Abu 'Abd Allah ibn Mujahid, and the discussion continued between them until the dawn broke, and the argument of al-Qadi prevailed over him, may Allah have mercy on them. And Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi al-Hanbali used to say to his companions: Hold fast to this man, for the Sunnah will never be free from need of him.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage narrates a significant event when Imam al-Baqillani arrived in Baghdad. He was invited by the Hanbali scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi, who was a leading figure of his time. A debate on ijtihad occurred between al-Baqillani and Abu 'Abd Allah ibn Mujahid, lasting until dawn. Al-Baqillani's argument prevailed, and al-Tamimi thereafter urged his companions to cling to him, stating that the Sunnah would never be independent of him. This highlights al-Baqillani's authority even among scholars of other madhhabs.

Key Terms
مسئلة الاجتهاد
ابن مجاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani's debate win over Ibn Mujahid demonstrated his scholarly authority, earning the respect of even those from opposing madhhabs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Life of Imam al-Baqillani

The Miraculous Time Expansion for al-Baqillani's Writings
Al-Baqillani's nightly 35-page writing and the divine time expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the miraculous time expansion granted to Imam al-Baqillani as a result of his sincere devotion, enabling his extraordinary productivity.

Core Idea
Sincere devotion can bring divine blessings that expand time itself.

Imam al-Baqillani's output of written works was so immense that later scholars reported a nightly routine of composing thirty-five pages from memory. This passage recounts the tradition that his books were distributed across his days, each day ten pages, and attributes this to a divine expansion of time—a miracle akin to the sun being delayed. Let's examine this remarkable claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of al-Baqillani's nightly writing
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the specific numbers: nightly 35 pages, daily distribution of 10 pages.
The passage also mentions the time expansion miracle.
2
Consider the theological explanation
The author attributes this productivity to divine intervention: Allah expanded time for him due to his sincerity. Reflect on the examples given (sun delay).
This is a form of karamah (divine favor).
3
Connect to the broader theme
This miracle supports the idea that sincere devotion can lead to extraordinary outcomes. How does this relate to al-Baqillani's role as a defender of orthodoxy?
Think about how his productivity served his mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تواليفه لقد روى كثير من المترجمين أن الإمام كان كل ليلة إذا صلى العشاء وقضى ورده وضع الدواة بين يديه وكتب خمساً وثلاثين ورقة تصنيفاً من حفظه وأن كتبه جمعت وقسمت على أيام حياته، فخص كل يوم منها عشر ورقات فلا شك وريب أن الله قد أوسع له الوقت لصدقه وإخلاصه بالعطاء فالله قادر على كل شيء فقد أخر الله الشمس عن وقت مغيبها مرات في أزمنة وأصقاع عديدة والله يبارك في الساعات لمن يشاء إذا كان الإمام كثير التأليف فكان أكثر ما صنفه في الرد على الفرق المخالفين لعقيدة أهل السنة والجماعة كما يقول ابن العماد في الشذرات أنه صنف تصانيف واسعة في الرد على الفرق الضالة وكما روى ابن عساكر أن الإمام له التصانيف الكثيرة في الرد على المخالفين من الرافضة والمعتزلة والجهمية والخوارج وغيرهم. وهناك قرينة (۱) انظر تبيين كذب المفتري ص / ۲۲۰، ۲۲۱، ۲۲۲.
His works: Many biographers have narrated that the Imam used to, every night after praying 'Isha and completing his litany, place the inkwell before him and write thirty-five pages of composition from his memory, and that his books were collected and distributed over the days of his life, so that each day had ten pages from them. There is no doubt that Allah expanded time for him due to his truthfulness and sincerity in giving. For Allah is powerful over everything. He has delayed the sun from its setting time multiple times in many eras and regions. And Allah blesses hours for whomever He wills. Since the Imam was prolific in authorship, most of what he composed was in refutation of the sects opposing the creed of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a. As Ibn al-'Imad says in al-Shadharat, he composed extensive works refuting the deviant sects. And as Ibn 'Asakir narrated, the Imam had many works refuting the opponents among the Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. And there is an indication (1) see Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari, pp. 220-222.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage summarizes the extraordinary output of Imam al-Baqillani. It repeats the nightly writing routine and adds that his collected works were divided so that each day of his life received ten pages. The author then attributes this productivity to divine time expansion as a reward for his sincerity, citing miracles of the sun being delayed. It emphasizes that most of his writings were refutations of sects that opposed Ahl al-Sunna, specifically naming Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. The passage cites Ibn al-'Imad and Ibn 'Asakir as sources for this information.

Key Terms
تواليف
صدق
إخلاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Baqillani's productivity was purely due to his own effort and discipline.
Correction: The passage explicitly attributes his output to divine expansion of time as a reward for his sincerity and truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many pages did al-Baqillani write each night?
A) 10
B) 35
C) 50
D) 100

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Baqillani's extraordinary writing output was a result of divine time expansion, a miracle granted due to his sincerity and devotion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah can expand your time if you are sincere? When you complain about having no time, have you ever examined the sincerity of your intentions and the quality of your devotion to Him? What would you need to change about your nightly routine to invite such a blessing into your life?
?
Al-Baqillani wrote 35 pages from memory every night after his litany. Is there a single act of worship or learning you do consistently every night with that level of dedication? If not, what is holding you back from starting tonight?
?
The source says 'Allah blesses hours for whom He wills.' Are you willing to be one of those people? What specific step will you take this week to increase your truthfulness and sincerity so that Allah might bless your time?

The Focus of al-Baqillani's Works: Refuting Deviant Sects
Al-Baqillani's works were mostly refutations of sects opposing Ahl al-Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that most of Imam al-Baqillani's writings were dedicated to refuting the sects that opposed the creed of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani's pen was a sword against deviant sects.

Having noted al-Baqillani's incredible productivity, the passage now clarifies the purpose of his works. It explicitly states that the majority of his compositions were refutations of groups that differed from Ahl al-Sunna. Scholars like Ibn al-'Imad and Ibn 'Asakir confirm that he wrote extensively against the Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. This lesson focuses on that defensive aspect of his legacy.

A Debate in Baghdad and Counsel to Adhere to Baqillani
Biographical anecdote about Baqillani's debate and endorsement by a Hanbali scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of a historic debate between Imam al-Baqillani and Ibn Mujahid, and the high esteem in which Baqillani was held by scholars of other schools.

Core Idea
A Hanbali leader declared, 'Hold fast to Baqillani—the Sunnah cannot do without him.'

This passage recounts a famous debate in Baghdad between Imam al-Baqillani and a scholar named Ibn Mujahid, witnessed by leading figures of the time. The story illustrates how Baqillani's theological method earned him respect even from scholars of different schools, such as the Hanbali imam Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi.

Guided Path

وعن عبد الله الحسين بن محمد الدامغاني قال : لما قدم القاضي الإمام أبو بكر الباقلاني بغداد دعاه الشيخ أبو الحسن التميمي الحنبلي رحمهما الله إمام عصره في مذهبه وشيخ مصره في رهطة وحضر الشيخ أبو عبد الله مجاهد والشيخ أبو الحسين محمد بن أحمد بن سمعون وأبو الحسن الفقيه فجرت مسئلة الاجتهاد بين القاضي أبي بكر وبين أبي عبد الله بن مجاهد وتعلق الكلام بينهما إلى أن انفجر عمود الصبح وظهر كلام القاضي عليه رحمهما الله وكان أبو الحسن التميمي الحنبلي يقول لأصحابه تمسكوا بهذا الرجل فليس للسنة عنه غنى أبداً.
And from Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Damaghani said: When the chief judge Abu Bakr al-Baqillani arrived in Baghdad, Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi al-Hanbali — may Allah have mercy on them — invited him, he being the imam of his time in his school and the shaykh of his city among his group. And Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Mujahid, Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Sam'un, and Abu al-Hasan al-Faqih were present. Then the issue of ijtihad arose between the judge Abu Bakr and Abu Abd Allah ibn Mujahid, and the discussion between them continued until the pillar of dawn broke, and the argument of the judge prevailed over him — may Allah have mercy on them. And Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi al-Hanbali used to say to his companions: 'Hold fast to this man, for the Sunnah has no independence from him ever.'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote recounting a debate between Imam al-Baqillani and another scholar, Ibn Mujahid, in Baghdad. The passage begins by reporting the tradition from al-Damaghani. It describes how al-Baqillani was invited by the Hanbali scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Tamimi, who was a leading authority of his time. The setting includes other prominent figures. The debate concerned the topic of ijtihad and lasted until dawn, with al-Baqillani's argument emerging triumphant. The passage concludes with al-Tamimi's instruction to his followers to adhere to al-Baqillani, stating that the Sunnah cannot do without him. This highlights the high regard al-Baqillani earned even from scholars of different methodological orientations, and affirms his role as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy.

The Prolific Writing of Imam al-Baqillani
Description of Baqillani's vast output and the divine blessing on his time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extraordinary scale of Imam al-Baqillani's scholarly output and how it was interpreted as a divine blessing and miracle of time-expansion.

Core Idea
Imam al-Baqillani's nightly thirty-five leaves: a sign of divine time-expansion.

Imam al-Baqillani was not just a theologian but a prodigious writer. Biographers record breathtaking numbers: thirty-five leaves per night from memory, seventy thousand leaves in refutation of atheists. This passage presents these claims and interprets them through the lens of divine blessing. Let's read the account and reflect on what it tells us about Baqillani's devotion and Allah's support for those who defend the truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the key numbers
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the numbers: thirty-five leaves per night, ten leaves per day, seventy thousand leaves. These numbers underscore the scale of his output.
The numbers are not mere statistics; they set up the miracle of time-expansion.
2
Understand the explanation for the productivity
The author states that this could only be due to Allah expanding time for him. Notice the examples given: the sun being delayed and Allah blessing hours for whom He wills. This is the core theological interpretation.
The author uses this explanation to affirm that Baqillani's work was divinely aided.
3
Identify the groups refuted
The passage lists the sects Baqillani refuted: Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. Note that this shows his role as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy.
This connects the immense output to his purpose: protecting the creed.
4
Reflect on the funeral proclamation
Read the anecdote about Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi's order. The titles proclaimed ('defender of the Sunnah', etc.) reinforce Baqillani's legacy and the reason for his vast writings.
The proclamation of 'seventy thousand leaves against atheists' is a climax.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقد روى كثير من المترجمين أن الإمام كان كل ليلة إذا صلى العشاء وقضى ورده وضع الدواة بين يديه وكتب خمساً وثلاثين ورقة تصنيفاً من حفظه وأن كتبه جمعت وقسمت على أيام حياته، فخص كل يوم منها عشر ورقات فلا شك وريب أن الله قد أوسع له الوقت لصدقه وإخلاصه بالعطاء فالله قادر على كل شيء فقد أخر الله الشمس عن وقت مغيبها مرات في أزمنة وأصقاع عديدة والله يبارك في الساعات لمن يشاء إذا كان الإمام كثير التأليف فكان أكثر ما صنفه في الرد على الفرق المخالفين لعقيدة أهل السنة والجماعة كما يقول ابن العماد في الشذرات أنه صنف تصانيف واسعة في الرد على الفرق الضالة وكما روى ابن عساكر أن الإمام له التصانيف الكثيرة في الرد على المخالفين من الرافضة والمعتزلة والجهمية والخوارج وغيرهم. وهناك قرينة أيضا تدل على ذلك وهو ما يذكره ابن عساكر أن الشيخ أبا الفضل التميمي يوم وفاته حضن العزاء حافياً مع إخوته وأصحابه وأمر أن ينادي بين يدي جنازته هذا ناصر السنة والدين هذا إمام المسلمين هذا الذي كان يذب عن الشريعة السنة المخالفين، هذا الذي صنّف سبعين ألف ورقة رداً على الملحدين.
Many biographers have narrated that the Imam, every night after praying Isha and completing his litany, would place the inkwell before him and write thirty-five leaves of composition from memory, and that his books were collected and distributed over the days of his life, so each day received ten leaves. There is no doubt that Allah had expanded time for him due to his truthfulness and sincerity in giving, for Allah is capable of everything. Indeed, Allah delayed the sun from its time of setting on multiple occasions in various eras and regions, and Allah blesses the hours for whomever He wills. Since the Imam was prolific in authorship, most of what he composed was in refutation of the groups opposing the creed of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. As Ibn al-Imad says in al-Shadharat, he composed extensive works in refutation of the misguided sects. And as Ibn Asakir narrated, the Imam has many works in refutation of opponents from the Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. There is also evidence indicating that — which Ibn Asakir mentions — that on the day of his death, Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi attended the condolence barefoot with his brothers and companions, and ordered that before his funeral it be proclaimed: 'This is the defender of the Sunnah and the religion! This is the imam of the Muslims! This is the one who defended the Sharia and the Sunnah against the opponents! This is the one who composed seventy thousand leaves in refutation of the atheists!'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Baqillani's extraordinary scholarly output. It begins by citing multiple biographers who report that Baqillani would write thirty-five leaves from memory every night after his night prayer and litany, and that his total writings, when divided over his lifespan, amounted to ten leaves per day. The author then asserts that this productivity could only be due to Allah's expansion of time for him, citing as analogies the miracles of the sun being delayed and Allah's general blessing of time. The passage then states the primary focus of his writings: refutation of sects opposing Sunni creed, specifically naming Rawafid, Mu'tazila, Jahmiyya, Khawarij, and others. This is corroborated by Ibn al-Imad and Ibn Asakir. The passage concludes with a striking anecdote from Ibn Asakir about the funeral of Baqillani, where Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi ordered the proclamation of his titles as defender of Sunnah and religion, and mentioned that he wrote seventy thousand leaves against atheists. This reinforces the theme of his massive, divinely-aided output in defense of orthodoxy.

الرد
أهل السنة والجماعة
الملحدين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the claim of thirty-five leaves a night is exaggeration or impossible without divine intervention.
Correction: The author treats it as a divine expansion of time and a miracle of barakah, not a natural human achievement.

?

The Legacy of Imam al-Baqillani's Works
Biographical and bibliographical listing of Baqillani's works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope and significance of Imam al-Baqillani's major works, particularly his defense of Sunni orthodoxy and his extensive writings on the inimitability of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Baqillani authored seventy thousand pages to defend the Sunnah against heresy.

Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani was a towering figure in Sunni theology and jurisprudence, known for his tireless refutation of heretical groups. This passage from a biographical source lists many of his key works, giving us a glimpse into his scholarly output and the high regard in which later scholars held him. As we explore this list, we will see how his writings shaped the defense of Sunni Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening account
Begin with the story of Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi's funeral, which sets the tone for Baqillani's legacy as a defender of the Sunnah.
Notice the title 'Nasser al-Sunnah' (Supporter of the Sunnah).
2
Identify the books listed
As you read the list of books, note the variety of topics: refutation of heresies, fiqh, imamate, and more. Pay attention to the external references (e.g., Ibn 'Asakir, al-Subki, Ibn Kathir).
3
Focus on Hidayat al-Mustarshidin
The passage gives a detailed description of the surviving manuscript of 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin'. Notice its size, content, and the emphasis on i'jaz al-Qur'an.
This work is said to be larger and more detailed than his separate book on i'jaz.
4
Reflect on Baqillani's method
The passage quotes Baqillani's description of the Batiniyya. Consider how his works exposed and refuted heretical groups systematically.

أيضا تدل على ذلك وهو ما يذكره ابن عساكر أن الشيخ أبا الفضل التميمي يوم وفاته حضن العزاء حافياً مع إخوته وأصحابه وأمر أن ينادي بين يدي جنازته هذا ناصر السنة والدين هذا إمام المسلمين هذا الذي كان يذب عن الشريعة السنة المخالفين، هذا الذي صنّف سبعين ألف ورقة رداً على الملحدين . وله [؟] لاية [؟] لقال [؟]
أما أسماء هذه الكتب فمنها ما ذكرها الإمام في كتابه هذا الذي بين أيدينا منها: كتاب كيفية الاستشهاد في الرد على أهل الجحد والعناد . كتاب الأصول الكبير في الفقه وذكره في هداية المسترشدين وأشار إليه أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في كتاب التبصير ص ۱۹۳ . كتاب مناقب الأئمة أو الإمامة الكبير ذكره في هداية المسترشدين في ذكر آية انشقاق القمر؛ حيث يقول: وقد تقصينا القول في ذلك في كتاب الإمامة بما يغني متأمله وهو كتاب حافل بين فيه ما جرى بين الصحابة وذكره حاجي خليفة ص ١٨٤١ . الكتاب الكفار المتأولين ذكره في باب ذكر ما يوجب خلع الإمام وسقوط [؟] من الفضاعته. حيث يقول: وقد ذكرنا ما في هذا الباب، في كتاب الكفار المتأولين. وله [؟] كتاب كشف الاستار في الرد على الباطنية. وقد ذكر السبكي في طبقاته في ترجمة محمد بن الموفق بن سعيد بن علي بن حسن بن ما بقي [؟] [؟] عبد الله الجنوشاني حيث يقول: وقد بين نسبهم جماعة منهم أبو بكر [؟] الباقلاني فإنه كشف [؟] في كتابه المسمى بكشف الأسرار الباطنية [؟] بطلان [؟] نسبة هؤلاء إلى الإمام علي كرم الله وجهه وذكره ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية ١٢ / ٣٥٠ في ترجمة القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني حيث ذكر مصنفاته وقال من أحسنها كتابه في الرد على الباطنية الذي سماه كشف الأسرار وهتك الأستار وذكره في صفحة ٣٤٦ في ترجمة علي بن محمد بن الحسين بن يوسف؛ حيث يقول: وقد صنف القاضي الباقلاني كتاباً في الرد على هؤلاء وسماه كشف الأسرار وهتك الأستار بين فيه فضائحهم وقبائحهم، ووضع أمرهم لكل أحد ووضوح أمرهم ينبئ عن مطاوي أفعالهم وأقوالهم، وقد كان الباقلاني يقول في عبارته عنهم: هم قوم يظهرون الرفض ويبطنون الكفر المحض. وذكر حاجي خليفة: ٦ - كتاب الملل والنحل ذكره حاجي خليفة . ٧ - كتاب هداية المسترشدين و المقنع في معرفة أصول الدين ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في التبصير ص ۱۹۳ . ولم يبق من هذا الكتاب سوى مجلد وهو في مكتبة الأزهر يحتوي على ٢٤٨ ورقة كتبه محمد بن عبد الله العدوي، بمدينة صور في سنة ٤٥٩ وقد أصاب التلف في أوراق عديدة من الكتاب ويشتمل هذا المجلد على أحد عشر جزءاً من تجزئة المؤلف، تبتدىء بأول الجزء السادس وتنتهي بانتهاء الجزء السابع عشر وهذه الأجزاء كلها مقصورة على القول في النبوات وأهم ما فيها وأروعه تلك الأبحاث الجليلة الطويلة، التي أدار الباقلاني الكلام فيها على إعجاز القرآن وملأ بها ستاً وخمسين ومائة ورقة وهي أكبر حجماً من كتاب إعجاز القرآن وأغزر مادة وأكثر تفصيلا، وأعمق بحثاً، وأدق بياناً . ٨ - كتاب نقض النقض ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في التبصير ص ۱۹۳ . ٩ - كتاب الفرق بين معجزات النبيين وكرامات الصالحين ذكره في هداية المسترشدين حيث يقول: وقد بينا في كتاب الفرق بين معجزات النبيين وكرامات الصالحين معنى وصف النبي أنه نبي وأن من الناس من قال: إنه مشتق ومأخوذ من الإنباء عن الأشياء والإخبار عن الله عزّ وجلّ .
Also indicating that is what Ibn 'Asakir mentions: that Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi on his death day attended the funeral barefoot with his brothers and companions and ordered that it be proclaimed before his bier: 'This is the supporter of the Sunnah and the religion, this is the Imam of the Muslims, this is the one who defended the Shari'ah and the Sunnah against the dissenters, this is the one who authored seventy thousand pages in refutation of the atheists.' And he has [?] ...
As for the names of these books, among them are those which the Imam mentioned in this book of his which is in our hands: the book 'Kayfiyyat al-Istishhad fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Jahd wa al-'Inad.' The book 'al-Usul al-Kabir' in fiqh, and he mentioned it in 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' and Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini referred to it in the book 'al-Tabsir' p. 193. The book 'Manaqib al-A'immah' or 'al-Imamah al-Kabir,' he mentioned it in 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' in the mention of the verse of the splitting of the moon; where he says: 'We have detailed the discussion on that in the book of al-Imamah, sufficient for the one who ponders it, and it is a comprehensive book in which he explained what occurred among the Companions,' and Haji Khalifa mentioned it p. 1841. The book 'al-Kuffar al-Mu'tawwilun' he mentioned in the chapter on what necessitates the deposition of the Imam and the fall of [?] from his [؟]. Where he says: 'We have mentioned what is in this chapter in the book al-Kuffar al-Mu'tawwilun.' And he has [?] the book 'Kashf al-Astar fi al-Radd 'ala al-Batiniyya.' And al-Subki mentioned in his Tabaqat in the biography of Muhammad ibn al-Muwaffaq ibn Sa'id ibn 'Ali ibn Hasan ibn ma baqi [?] [?] 'Abdallah al-Jannushani where he says: 'A group of them clarified their lineage, including Abu Bakr [?] al-Baqillani, for he revealed [?] in his book named 'Kashf al-Asrar al-Batiniyya' [?] the falsehood of [?] the attribution of these to Imam 'Ali, may Allah honor his face.' And Ibn Kathir mentioned in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya 12/350 in the biography of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani where he mentioned his works and said: 'Among the best of them is his book in refutation of the Batiniyya which he named 'Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar.'' And he mentioned it on p. 346 in the biography of 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Yusuf; where he says: 'Al-Qadi al-Baqillani authored a book in refutation of these and named it 'Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar,' in which he explained their scandals and abominations, and exposed their affair to everyone, and the clarity of their affair indicates the details of their deeds and sayings.' And al-Baqillani used to say in his description of them: 'They are a people who manifest rafd (rejection) and conceal pure disbelief.' And Haji Khalifa mentioned: 6 - The book 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal,' mentioned by Haji Khalifa. 7 - The book 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' and 'al-Muqni' fi Ma'rifat Usul al-Din,' mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in al-Tabsir p. 193. And nothing remains of this book except one volume, which is in the al-Azhar library, containing 248 folios, written by Muhammad ibn 'Abdallah al-'Adawi in the city of Sur in the year 459, and many pages of the book have been affected by damage. And this volume comprises eleven parts of the author's division, starting from the beginning of the sixth part and ending at the end of the seventeenth part, and all these parts are confined to the discussion on prophecies, and the most important and most magnificent of what they contain are those long, lofty researches in which al-Baqillani conducted the discussion on the inimitability of the Qur'an, and he filled with them one hundred and fifty-six folios, and it is larger in size than the book 'I'jaz al-Qur'an,' more abundant in material, more detailed, deeper in investigation, and more precise in exposition. 8 - The book 'Naqd al-Naqd,' mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in al-Tabsir p. 193. 9 - The book 'al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin,' he mentioned it in 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' where he says: 'We have explained in the book 'al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin' the meaning of describing the Prophet as a prophet, and that among people are those who say it is derived and taken from al-inba' (informing) about things and reporting about Allah, Mighty and Majestic.'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical note listing the works of Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. It begins by quoting Ibn 'Asakir's account of Shaykh Abu al-Fadl al-Tamimi's funeral, where the deceased was praised as a defender of the Sunnah and religion, linking Baqillani's own efforts to that tradition. The passage then enumerates several of Baqillani's books, many of which were written in refutation of various heretical groups. The author mentions that Baqillani is said to have written seventy thousand pages against atheists. The list includes: 'Kayfiyyat al-Istishhad fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Jahd wa al-'Inad' (a method of testifying against the stubborn), 'al-Usul al-Kabir' (a major work on usul al-fiqh), 'Manaqib al-A'immah' or 'al-Imamah al-Kabir' (on the imamate and early disputes), 'al-Kuffar al-Mu'tawwilun' (on those who exceeded bounds), and 'Kashf al-Astar fi al-Radd 'ala al-Batiniyya' (exposing the secrets of the Batinis). The passage provides external references: al-Subki's Tabaqat and Ibn Kathir's al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya endorse Baqillani's works, especially his refutation of the Batiniyya. Ibn Kathir describes 'Kashf al-Asrar wa Hatk al-Astar' as one of his best works, exposing the scandals of the Batinis. Baqillani's own description of them as 'people who manifest rafd and conceal pure disbelief' is quoted. The passage then continues with Haji Khalifa's mention of 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' and the important work 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' and 'al-Muqni' fi Ma'rifat Usul al-Din'. A detailed description of the surviving manuscript of 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' is given: a single volume in al-Azhar containing 248 folios, written in 459 AH, comprising parts six through seventeen, all focused on prophethood, with extensive discussion on the inimitability of the Qur'an (i'jaz), filling 156 folios. This part is said to be larger and more detailed than Baqillani's separate work 'I'jaz al-Qur'an'. Finally, two more books are listed: 'Naqd al-Naqd' (a refutation of a refutation) and 'al-Farq bayn Mu'jizat al-Nabiyyin wa Karamat al-Salihin' (distinguishing miracles of prophets from wonders of saints), which discusses the meaning of being a prophet.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Baqillani authored numerous works defending Sunni orthodoxy, with his Hidayat al-Mustarshidin containing an unparalleled treatment of the Qur'an's inimitability.

Manuscript of Hidayat al-Mustarshidin and al-Muqni'
Describes extant manuscript of two works focusing on prophethood and Qur'anic inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the manuscript evidence for Baqillani's works on prophethood and the significance of his treatment of i'jaz al-Qur'an.

Core Idea
Baqillani's manuscript on prophethood contains his most detailed i'jaz analysis.

This passage provides a glimpse into the surviving manuscript of two of Imam al-Baqillani's theological works. The description highlights that the only extant volume focuses entirely on prophethood, with a substantial portion dedicated to the inimitability of the Qur'an. This reveals the centrality of i'jaz in his defense of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the manuscript description
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the manuscript's physical details and content. Then read the translation to confirm understanding.
Pay attention to the year and location of copying.
2
Identify the two works
The passage mentions two titles. Understand that they likely refer to the same work or a combined work, not two separate books.
The common misunderstanding is that they are distinct.
3
Note the i'jaz section's importance
The passage emphasizes that the volume's most significant part is the lengthy treatment of i'jaz al-Qur'an, which is more detailed than Baqillani's separate book on the topic.
This underscores the centrality of i'jaz in proving prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب «هداية المسترشدين» و «المقنع في معرفة أصول الدين ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في التبصير ص ۱۹۳ . ولم يبق من هذا الكتاب سوى مجلد وهو في مكتبة الأزهر يحتوي على ٢٤٨ ورقة كتبه محمد بن عبد الله العدوي، بمدينة صور في سنة ٤٥٩ وقد أصاب التلف في أوراق عديد من الكتاب ويشتمل هذا المجلد على أحد عشر جزءاً من تجزئة المؤلف، تبتدىء بأول الجزء السادس وتنتهي بانتهاء الجزء السابع عشر وهذه الأجزاء كلها مقصورة على القول في النبوات وأهم ما فيها وأروعه تلك الأبحاث الجليلة الطويلة، التي أدار الباقلاني الكلام فيها على إعجاز القرآن وملأ بها ستاً وخمسين ومائة ورقة وهي أكبر حجماً من كتاب إعجاز القرآن واغزر ،مادة وأكثر تفصيلا، وأعمق بحثاً، وأدق بياناً .
The book 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' and 'al-Muqni' fi Ma'rifat Usul al-Din' mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in al-Tabsir p. 193. And nothing remains of this book except one volume, and it is in the Azhar library, containing 248 folios, written by Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Adawi in the city of Sur in the year 459. And damage has affected many pages of the book. And this volume comprises eleven parts of the author's division, beginning with the first part of the sixth part and ending with the end of the seventeenth part. And these parts are entirely confined to the discourse on prophecies (al-nubuwwat). And the most important and most magnificent of what is in it are those great lengthy investigations in which al-Baqillani directed the discussion to the inimitability of the Qur'an (i'jaz al-Qur'an), and he filled with them one hundred and fifty-six folios. And it is larger in size than the book 'I'jaz al-Qur'an', and more abundant in material, more detailed, deeper in research, and more precise in exposition.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a description of two of Baqillani's works, 'Hidayat al-Mustarshidin' and 'al-Muqni' fi Ma'rifat Usul al-Din', as referenced by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini. It provides manuscript details: only one volume survives, housed in the Azhar library, containing 248 folios, copied by Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Adawi in Sur in the year 459 AH. The volume includes parts 6 through 17 of the author's original division, and all these parts are devoted exclusively to the topic of prophethood (al-nubuwwat). The most significant portion is a lengthy treatment of the inimitability of the Qur'an (i'jaz al-Qur'an) spanning 156 folios. This treatment is said to be larger, more detailed, deeper, and more precise than Baqillani's own separate work 'I'jaz al-Qur'an'. This highlights Baqillani's extensive engagement with the doctrine of i'jaz and its central place in his defense of prophethood.

Correction: They are likely two titles referring to the same work or a combined work, as the passage uses 'and' and refers to 'this book' in the singular.

Kitab al-Intisar: Defending the Transmission of the Qur'an
Introduction to Kitab al-Intisar and its objectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose and scope of Imam al-Baqillani's work 'Kitab al-Intisar' in defending the integrity of the Qur'anic text against various allegations.

Core Idea
Al-Intisar systematically refutes all allegations against the Qur'an's transmission and content.

Imam al-Baqillani wrote 'Kitab al-Intisar' as a comprehensive defense of the Qur'an's flawless transmission. This lesson introduces you to the book's purpose and the types of allegations it addresses, as described by the author himself. You will see how the work is structured to refute claims of alteration, contradiction, and textual corruption.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening description
The passage begins with the book's title and purpose: defending the Qur'an's transmission. Notice the key phrase 'لصحة نقل القرآن' (for the correctness of the transmission of the Qur'an).
2
Identify the allegations listed
The introduction lists multiple allegations against the Qur'an. Find them and note the variety – from claims of alteration to grammatical errors.
Some allegations are from atheists, others from sectarians.
3
Trace the book's structure
The passage outlines the book's chapters: transmission of readings, virtues of caliphs, compilation of the Qur'an, refutation of anomalous reports, and response to atheists and Rafida.
This shows a methodical, layered defense.
4
Connect to broader context
Understand that this work is one of the earliest systematic defenses of the Qur'an's authenticity, prefiguring later 'Uloom al-Qur'an.'
Consider why such a work was necessary in Baqillani's time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 - كتاب الانتصار لصحة نقل القرآن والرد على من نحله الفساد بزيادة أو نقصان وقد قال في مقدمته: «أما بعد فقد وقفت تولى الله عصمتكم وأحسن هدايتكم وتوفيقكم على ما ذكرتموه من شدة حاجتكم إلى الكلام القرآن وإقامة البرهان على استفاضة ،أمره، وإحاطة السلف بعلمه وانقطاع العذر في نقله وقيام الحجة على الخلق به وإبطال ما يدعيه أهل الضلال من تحريفه وتغييره ودخول الخلل فيه وذهاب شيء كثير منه وزيادة أمور فيه وما يدعيه أهل الإلحاد وشيعتهم من منتحلي الإسلام من تناقض كثير منه وخلو بعضه من الفائدة وكونه غير متناسب وما ذكروه من فساد النظم ودخول اللحن فيه وركاكة التكرار، وقلة البيان وتأخير المقدم وتقديم المؤخر إلى غير ذلك من وجوه مطاعنهم. وذكر جمل مما روي من الحروف الزائدة والقراءات المخالفة لمصحف الجماعة، والإبانة عن وهاء نقل ذلك وضعفه وأن الحجة لم تقم بشيء منه وعرف ما وضعتموه من كثرة استضرار الضعفاء بتمويههم وعظم موقع الاستبصار والانتفاع بنقض شبههم . ونحن بحول الله وعونه نأتي بجمل تزيل الريب والشبهة وتوقف الواضعة، ثم بدأ بالكلام في نقل القراءات وقيام الحجة به ووصف توفر همم الأمة على نقله وحياطته ثم ذكر مناقب أبي بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان وبيان جمعه للقرآن وكشف الأكاذيب من الروايات الشاذة عن عمر وعثمان وعلي وأبي وعبد الله بن مسعود وغير ذلك مما حصل أيام عثمان ثم يقول: ونصف جملاً من مطاعن الملحدين واتباعهم من الرافضة في كتاب الله عزّ وجلّ ونكشف عن تمويه الفريقين بما يوضح الحق. ونذكر في كل فصل من هذه الفصول بمشيئة الله وتوفيقه ما فيه بلاغ للمهتدين، وشفاء وتبصرة للمسترشدين توخياً لطاعة الله جل وعزّ ورغبة من جزيل ثوابه وما توفيقنا إلا بالله وهو المستعان . وقد ذكره في «هداية المسترشدين حيث يقول: «وقد ذكرنا في كِتَاب الانتصار لصحة نقل القرآن جميع مطاعن الملحدة وكل من الملة على القرآن، وكشفنا عن فساد توهمهم وتمويههم ودعواهم لتناقض آيات منه واختلافهم ؛ وما طعنوا به من كثرة التكرار.
1 - The book of al-Intisar for the correctness of the transmission of the Qur'an and the refutation of those who ascribe corruption to it by increase or decrease. And he said in its introduction: 'To proceed: I have come to know—may God take care of your infallibility and improve your guidance and success—what you mentioned of your severe need for discourse on the Qur'an and establishing the proof of its widespread transmission, the comprehensiveness of the predecessors in knowledge of it, the cutting off of excuse regarding its transmission, the establishment of the argument against creation by it, and the nullification of what the people of misguidance claim of alteration and change, the occurrence of defect in it, the loss of much of it, and the addition of matters in it, and what the people of atheism and their sects from among the pretenders to Islam claim of much contradiction in it, the lack of benefit of some of it, its lack of proportionality, and what they mentioned of corruption of composition, the occurrence of grammatical error in it, feebleness of repetition, lack of clarity, delaying of the antecedent, and advancing of the consequent, and other such aspects of their allegations. And he mentioned a number of what has been transmitted of superfluous letters and readings contrary to the Mushaf of the community, and the exposition of the weakness and feebleness of that transmission, and that the proof is not established by any of it, and he recognized what you set forth of the great harm to the weak by their obfuscation and the great importance of insight and benefit in refuting their doubts. And we, by the power of God and His assistance, bring a number of matters that remove doubt and uncertainty and halt the obfuscator. Then he began with speech on the transmission of readings and the establishment of the proof by it, and the description of the abundance of the nation's endeavors in its transmission and preservation, then he mentioned the virtues of Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then 'Uthman, and the explanation of his compilation of the Qur'an, and the exposure of lies from anomalous reports about 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, Ubayy, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and other matters that occurred during the days of 'Uthman. Then he says: 'And we will enumerate a number of the allegations of the atheists and their followers from the Rafida against the Book of God, Mighty and Majestic, and we will uncover the obfuscation of both parties by clarifying the truth. And we will mention in each chapter of these chapters, by the will of God and His success, what suffices for the guided, and healing and insight for the seekers, seeking the obedience of God, Great and Majestic, and desiring His abundant reward. And our success is only from God, and He is the One sought for help.' And he mentioned it in 'Hidaya al-Mustarshidin' where he says: 'We have mentioned in the book of al-Intisar for the correctness of the transmission of the Qur'an all the allegations of the atheists and everyone from the nation against the Qur'an, and we have uncovered the corruption of their delusions and obfuscations and their claim of contradiction between its verses and their disagreement, and what they attacked by of frequent repetition.'”
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic entry describing al-Baqillani's work 'Kitab al-Intisar'. It begins by stating the title and overarching purpose: defending the correct transmission of the Qur'an against claims of corruption by addition or deletion. Then it quotes the book's introduction at length. The introduction acknowledges the readers' need for a discourse on the Qur'an that establishes proofs for its widespread transmission, the predecessors' mastery, and the conclusive argument it provides against humanity. It then lists the allegations of various groups: alteration, change, loss, additions, contradictions, lack of benefit, disproportionality, poor composition, grammatical errors, feeble repetition, lack of clarity, and misplaced order. It also addresses claims about superfluous letters and deviant readings, exposing their weakness. The author then outlines the structure: discussing the transmission of readings, the virtues of the early caliphs (Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman) and the compilation of the Qur'an, refuting anomalous reports, then addressing the allegations of atheists and the Rafida. The entry concludes by noting that this work is cited in 'Hidaya al-Mustarshidin', where it says that the book covers all the allegations of atheists and others against the Qur'an and exposes their falsity, including claims of contradiction and excessive repetition. The description highlights the comprehensive scope of the work in defending the integrity of the Qur'anic text.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kitab al-Intisar is widely available in complete form.
Correction: The work is often cited but not widely extant; only fragments remain. This description is based on the author's own introduction and later citations.

Al-Baqillani's Kitab Daqa'iq al-Kalam: A Bibliographic Puzzle
Bibliographic entry with two possible identifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity and sources of al-Baqillani's 'Kitab Daqa'iq al-Kalam' and why its title may be confused with another work.

Core Idea
Medieval book titles can be ambiguous and lead to scholarly detective work.

This passage introduces us to a book by Imam al-Baqillani, a major Ash'ari theologian. The title suggests it deals with subtle points of theology and refutes opponents, but a question arises: is it the same as another title mentioned by Ibn Kathir? Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once for overall meaning, then the translation. Notice the full title and the two sources cited.
The title itself indicates the book's purpose: refutation of opponents.
2
Identify the two sources mentioning the book
One source is 'Hidaya al-Mustarshidin' and the other is Ibn Kathir's 'al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya'. Note what each says about the book and the alternate title 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq'.
Ibn Kathir suggests the two works might be the same, but the author leaves it open.
3
Reflect on the ambiguity
Consider why scholars might be unsure if two titles refer to the same work. Think about how books were copied and named in pre-modern times.
This ambiguity is common in classical Islamic bibliographic history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
11 - كتاب دقائق الكلام والرد على من خالف الحق من الأوائل ومنتحلي الإسلام ذكره في هداية المسترشدين». وذكـره أيضاً ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية ٣٥٠/١١ أن للباقلاني كتاباً اسمه «دقائق الحقائق» فلعله يكون هو ولعله غيره .
11 - The book of Subtleties of Speech and the Refutation of Those Who Oppose the Truth from the Ancients and the Adherents of Islam, mentioned in 'Hidaya al-Mustarshidin'. And it is also mentioned by Ibn Kathir in 'al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya' 11/350 that al-Baqillani has a book named 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq', and perhaps it is the same, or perhaps it is different.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a brief bibliographic entry for another work by al-Baqillani. It gives the full title, which indicates the work deals with subtle points of theology (kalam) and refutes those who oppose the truth, including early groups and those who claim to be Muslims. It then cites two sources: 'Hidaya al-Mustarshidin' (likely by al-Baqillani himself or a later author) and Ibn Kathir's historical work 'al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya'. Ibn Kathir notes that al-Baqillani wrote a book called 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq' (Subtleties of Realities) and suggests it might be the same as 'Daqa'iq al-Kalam' or perhaps a distinct work. The entry leaves this identification open.

هداية المسترشدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'Daqa'iq al-Kalam' and 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq' are definitely the same book.
Correction: The passage only says 'perhaps it is the same, or perhaps it is different'; the identification is uncertain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author humbly admits he does not know for sure. Are you willing to admit 'I don't know' when studying your religion, or do you feel pressured to have a firm answer? Think of a question you've always wanted to ask but were afraid to admit you didn't know. Will you seek clarity today?
?

Al-Baqillani's Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad in Usul al-Fiqh
Bibliographic entry for al-Baqillani's usul work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the bibliographic context of al-Baqillani's work 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' in the field of usul al-fiqh as recorded by a later scholar.

Core Idea
A single bibliographic entry can illuminate an author's scholarly output.

This lesson introduces a brief but important piece of evidence for al-Baqillani's contributions to usul al-fiqh. The entry, preserved by a later Shafi'i scholar, confirms the existence and title of his work 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad.' While short, such references help reconstruct the intellectual legacy of early Islamic scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text of the bibliographic entry and its English translation. Note the exact phrasing and the source cited.
The passage is very concise but contains key information.
2
Identify the work and its field
The title 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad fi Usul al-Fiqh' explicitly states it is a work on principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh). Understand the significance of al-Baqillani writing in this field.
Al-Baqillani was primarily known for kalam, but he also wrote on usul.
3
Note the source of the reference
The entry is attributed to Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfara'ini in his book 'al-Tabsir' on page 193. Consider why such secondary sources are valuable for historical research.
Al-Isfara'ini was a Shafi'i scholar, indicating cross-madhhab citation.

The source is 'al-Tabsir' by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfara'ini, a Shafi'i scholar, who mentions it on page 193. No further details are given.

Key Terms
التقريب والإرشاد
أصول الفقه
التبصير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' is the same as al-Baqillani's other usul work 'al-Intisar'.
Correction: They are distinct works; the title 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' is specifically mentioned by al-Isfara'ini and is not to be confused with 'al-Intisar'.

Checkpoint

D) Hadith criticism

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani's 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' is a work on usul al-fiqh, preserved through a citation by a later scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a single citation can keep a work alive in scholarly memory for centuries, what does that suggest about the weight of your own references and attributions? Do you take care to accurately credit the sources you use?
?
Consider that al-Baqillani's work is known to us only through a brief mention by another scholar. How does the fragility of knowledge transmission affect your appreciation of the texts you study today?
?
When you learn a piece of Islamic knowledge, do you feel a responsibility to preserve and transmit it accurately? How does this lesson's example challenge your personal commitment to scholarly integrity?

Al-Baqillani's Refutation of Four Sects
Bibliographic entry listing a refutation work against four sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of al-Baqillani's work refuting four major theological sects and the context of these groups.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani's refutation work targeted four key sects: Rafida, Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Jahmiyya.

Al-Baqillani wrote a work specifically to refute the beliefs of four influential theological groups. This lesson introduces the work and provides background on each sect, drawing from a brief bibliographic entry.

Guided Path

Commentary
This passage is another brief bibliographic entry. It lists a work by al-Baqillani that refutes four major theological sects: the Rafida (a pejorative term for Shia who reject the first three caliphs), the Mu'tazila (rationalist theologians), the Khawarij (an early seceder group), and the Jahmiyya (followers of Jahm ibn Safwan who held extreme negating views on divine attributes). The source is al-Safadi's biographical dictionary 'al-Wafi bi al-Wafayat', vol. 3, page 177.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'Rafida' refers to all Shia indiscriminately.
Correction: The term 'Rafida' is a polemical label used specifically for Shia who reject the first three caliphs, not all Shia.

Imam al-Baqillani's Major Works: A Bibliography
This passage lists al-Baqillani's works with brief descriptions and two longer excerpts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will have a comprehensive overview of Imam al-Baqillani's major works and understand the breadth of his scholarly contributions across theology, law, and Qur'anic studies.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani's writings defend orthodoxy and explore the inimitability of the Qur'an.

This lesson presents a list of Imam al-Baqillani's most important writings, including his famous works on Qur'anic inimitability and polemics. The passage also contains a sample argument from his book al-Naqd al-Kabir, which refutes the sophistical denial of a beginning for the letters of the basmala. As you read, notice how each work addresses a different aspect of Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the full list of works
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. The list is numbered from 11 to 18, plus additional works mentioned after.
Pay attention to the diversity of subjects.
2
Identify the subject areas
Categorize each work by its subject: kalam, usul al-fiqh, Qur'anic studies, or polemics.
Some works may cover multiple areas.
3
Analyze the argument from al-Naqd al-Kabir
Examine the quoted passage in item 14. Al-Baqillani argues that if letters occur one after another, then the first has a beginning. Understand his logical refutation.
This demonstrates his method in kalam.
4
Reflect on the I'jaz al-Qur'an excerpt
In item 16, al-Baqillani criticizes earlier works on i'jaz. Why does he think his work is necessary?
Consider his emphasis on clarity and completeness.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خالف كتاب الانتصار لصحة نقل القرآن جميع مطاعن الملحدة وكل من الملة على القرآن، وكشفنا عن فساد توهمهم وتمويههم ودعواهم لتناقض آيات منه واختلافهم؛ وما طعنوا به من كثرة التكرار.

۱۱ ـ كتاب دقائق الكلام والرد على من خالف الحق من الأوائل ومنتحلي الإسلام ذكره في هداية المسترشدين. وذكره أيضاً ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية ١١/٣٥٠ أن للباقلاني كتاباً اسمه «دقائق الحقائق» فلعله يكون هو ولعله غيره.

۱۲ - كتاب التقريب والإرشاد في أصول الفقه ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في كتاب «التبصير» ص ۱۹۳.

۱۳ - كتاب «الكسب» ذكره أبو المظفر الاسفراييني في «التبصير» ص ۱۹۳.

١٤ - كتاب «النقض الكبير» ومنه هذا النص الذي أورده إمام الحرمين في الشامل قال أبو بكر الباقلاني في «النقض الكبير»: من زعم أن السين من الله بعد الباء والميم بعد السين الواقعة بعد الباء لا أول له فقد خرج عن المعقول، وجحد الضرورة وأنكر البديهة، فإن اعترف بوقوع شيء بعد شيء فقد اعترف بأوليته، فإن ادعى أنه لا أول له، فقد سقطت مما جنته وتعين لحوقه بالسفسطة. وكيف يرجى أن يرشد بالدليل من يتواقح في جحد الضروري.

١٥ - كتاب الرد على الرافضة والمعتزلة والخوارج والجهمية ذكره الصفدي في الوافي ٣/١٧٧.

ومن ثم كتاب الانصاف وهو المسمى برسالة الحرة وقد عني مركزنا بتحقيقه وكان قد سبق وحققه الشيخ محمد زاهد الكوثري وطبع بالقاهرة في سنة ١٣٦٩، وقد ذكر الباقلاني في أول مقدمته أما وفقت على ما التمسته الحرة الفاضلة الدينة أحسن الله توفيقها لما بعد. فقد

١٦ - كتاب إعجاز القرآن وهو من أجود ما ألف في هذا الفن وقد ذكر في مقدمته: إن الذين ألفوا في معاني القرآن من علماء اللغة والكلام لم يبسطوا القول في الإبانة عن وجه معجزته والدلالة على مكانه أن الحاجة إلى ذلك البيان أمس والاشتغال به أوجب فهو أحق بالتصنيف من الخبر والاعراض وغريب النحو وبديع الاعراب. وإن ما صنفه في هذا المعنى جاء غير كامل فربا به قد أقل بتهذيبه وأهمل ترتيبه، وقد التمس لبعضهم العذر فيما وقع منه من تفريط لأن بيان وجه الإعجاز مما لا يمكن بيانه إلا بعد التقدم في أمور عظيمة القدر، دقيقة المسلك، لطيفة المأخذ. وقال: إن الجاحظ «صنف في نظم القرآن كتاباً لم يزد فيه على ما قاله المتكلمون قبله ولم يكشف عما يلتبس في أكثر هذا المعنى.

وقد قام مركزنا بتحقيقه وكان قد سبق وطبع في مصر ونشرته دار المعارف بتحقيق الأستاذ أحمد صقر.

۱۷ - كتاب «التبصرة» ذكره ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية ١١/٣٥٠.

۱۸ - كتاب «شرح الإبانة» ذكره ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية ١١/٣٥٠ وغير ذلك من المجاميع الكبار والصغار.

وأما التمهيد وهو الذي بين أيدينا وهو كتاب في الرد على أهل البدع
The book al-Intisar for the correct transmission of the Qur'an [refutes] all the slanders of the heretics and everyone from the nation against the Qur'an, and we revealed the corruption of their illusion and deception and their claim of contradiction in its verses and their disagreement, and what they slandered by abundant repetition.

11 - The book Daa'iq al-Kalam wa al-Radd 'ala man Khalafa al-Haqq min al-Awa'il wa Muntahili al-Islam, mentioned in Hidaya al-Mustarshidin. Also mentioned by Ibn Kathir in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya (11/350) that al-Baqillani has a book called Daa'iq al-Haqa'iq; perhaps it is the same or perhaps it is different.

12 - The book al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad fi Usul al-Fiqh, mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in the book al-Tabsir p. 193.

13 - The book al-Kasb, mentioned by Abu al-Muzaffar al-Isfarayini in al-Tabsir p. 193.

14 - The book al-Naqd al-Kabir, from which comes this text cited by Imam al-Haramayn in al-Shamil. Abu Bakr al-Baqillani said in al-Naqd al-Kabir: Whoever claims that the letter sin from Allah after the ba and the mim after the sin occurring after the ba has no beginning, he has departed from reason, denied what is necessary, and rejected the self-evident. If he admits the occurrence of one thing after another, he has admitted its beginning. If he claims it has no beginning, he has fallen from [the truth] he perpetrated, and it is incumbent upon him to join the sophists. How can one who is so shameless in denying the necessary be guided by evidence?

15 - The book al-Radd 'ala al-Rafida wa al-Mu'tazila wa al-Khawarij wa al-Jahmiyya, mentioned by al-Safadi in al-Wafi (3/177).

Also, the book al-Insaf, which is called Risala al-Hurra. Our center undertook its verification and it was previously verified by Shaykh Muhammad Zahid al-Kawthari and printed in Cairo in 1369 AH. Al-Baqillani mentioned at the beginning of its introduction: "As for my success in what the virtuous, pious free woman requested—may Allah improve her success—for what followed."

16 - The book I'jaz al-Qur'an, which is among the best works composed in this art. He mentioned in its introduction: Those who authored on the meanings of the Qur'an from scholars of language and kalam did not elaborate in explaining the aspect of its inimitability and demonstrating its significance, despite the fact that the need for that explanation is more urgent and occupying oneself with it is more obligatory. It is more deserving of being a book than [works on] reports, declensions, rare grammar, and rhetorical figures. And what he composed in this regard came out incomplete, so perhaps he made it brief in its refinement and neglected its arrangement. He excused some of them for their negligence in what occurred from them because explaining the aspect of inimitability cannot be possible except after advancement in matters of great magnitude, subtle pathway, delicate methodology. He said: al-Jahiz authored a book on the composition of the Qur'an, but he added nothing beyond what the theologians before him said and did not uncover what is obscure in most of this subject.

Our center has verified it, and it was previously printed in Egypt and published by Dar al-Ma'arif with the verification of Professor Ahmad Saqr.

17 - The book al-Tabsira, mentioned by Ibn Kathir in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya (11/350).

18 - The book Sharh al-Ibana, mentioned by Ibn Kathir in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya (11/350), and other works both large and small.

As for al-Tamhid, which is in our hands, it is a book refuting the people of innovation.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing of the major works of Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. It begins with a brief description of the book 'Kitab al-Intisar' (The Book of Triumph), which defends the authenticity of the Qur'an against heretical attacks. Then follows a numbered list (from 11 to 18) of his other important writings. Each entry includes the title and often a brief comment, a citation from another scholar, or a quoted excerpt.

1. The first work mentioned is 'Kitab al-Intisar li Sihhat Naql al-Qur'an', described as a refutation of all slanders against the Qur'an, exposing the falsehoods of those who claim contradictions.

2. Item 11: 'Kitab Daqa'iq al-Kalam wa al-Radd 'ala man Khalafa al-Haqq' is referenced in Ibn Kathir's history, with a note that he also has a book called 'Daqa'iq al-Haqa'iq', possibly the same.

3. Item 12: 'Kitab al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad fi Usul al-Fiqh' is a work on usul al-fiqh, cited by al-Isfarayini.

4. Item 13: 'Kitab al-Kasb' is also noted by al-Isfarayini.

5. Item 14: 'Kitab al-Naqd al-Kabir' contains a significant passage quoted by Imam al-Haramayn. This passage refutes the sophistical idea that the letters of the basmala (bismillah) have no beginning. Al-Baqillani argues that admitting sequential occurrence necessarily implies a beginning, denying which leads to sophistry.

6. Item 15: 'Kitab al-Radd' lists polemical works against various sects: Rafida, Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Jahmiyya.

7. Then the passage adds 'Kitab al-Insaf' (also called Risala al-Hurra). It mentions that the modern center (publishing this edition) verified it, and it was previously edited by al-Kawthari. It includes the opening line of al-Baqillani's introduction, thanking a virtuous free woman who requested guidance.

8. Item 16: 'Kitab I'jaz al-Qur'an' is praised as one of the best works on Qur'anic inimitability. Al-Baqillani criticizes earlier scholars for not elaborating on this topic, noting that even al-Jahiz's book on nazm al-Qur'an did not go beyond previous theologians. He emphasizes the difficulty of explaining i'jaz, requiring advanced knowledge.

9. Item 17: 'Kitab al-Tabsira' is mentioned via Ibn Kathir.

10. Item 18: 'Kitab Sharh al-Ibana' is also cited via Ibn Kathir.

Finally, the passage identifies the present book, 'al-Tamhid', as a refutation of the people of innovation (ahl al-bida').

This list demonstrates the breadth of al-Baqillani's scholarship: kalam (dialectical theology), usul al-fiqh (legal theory), Qur'anic studies (i'jaz), and polemics against various sects. The detailed entry on 'al-Naqd al-Kabir' shows his method of argumentation, and the entry on 'I'jaz al-Qur'an' reveals his assessment of earlier works.

النقض الكبير
التمهيد
الانتصار
دقائق الكلام
التقريب والإرشاد
الرد على الرافضة
الانصاف
التبصرة
شرح الإبانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The letters of the basmala (bismillah) have no beginning.
Correction: Al-Baqillani argues that if letters occur sequentially, then the first has a beginning; denying this is sophistry.

Checkpoint
Which work by al-Baqillani is described as being about the inimitability of the Qur'an?
A) كتاب الانتصار
B) كتاب التقريب والإرشاد
C) كتاب إعجاز القرآن
D) كتاب النقض الكبير

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Baqillani authored works in multiple fields, with his most famous being on Qur'anic inimitability and his refutation of sophistry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about al-Baqillani's argument that denying the obvious sequence of letters is sophistry. What 'obvious' truths about Allah or His revelation are you tempted to rationalize away? Have you ever allowed doubt to creep in because you wanted to appear intellectually sophisticated? Will you repent from that and embrace the clear truth, even if it seems 'simple'?
?
Al-Baqillani criticized earlier scholars for not elaborating on the inimitability of the Qur'an. When was the last time you studied the Qur'an not just for meaning, but to experience its wonder? Are you satisfied with a superficial reading, or do you yearn to uncover the depth that proves it is from Allah? Commit today to reading a tafsir or work on i'jaz to deepen your conviction.
?
The free woman (al-hurra) sought guidance from al-Baqillani, and he responded with a book. Has there been a time when someone came to you with a sincere question about faith, and you dismissed it? Will you, like al-Baqillani, take the time to guide others, even if they are not scholars? What step will you take this week to share the truth with someone who is seeking?

Biographical Notes on Five Companions
Biographical entries for five companions mentioned in the argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of five companions referenced in Baqillani's argument, including their lineage, roles, and death dates.

Core Idea
Five companions—poet, diplomat, jurist, governor, and caliph—each played distinct roles in early Islam.

In the previous argument, Baqillani mentions several companions to support his reasoning. To fully appreciate his references, we need to identify who these individuals are. This lesson presents brief biographical entries for Abdullah ibn Rawaha, Amr ibn al-As, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Amr ibn Hazm, and Ali ibn Abi Talib. These profiles will help you connect the names to their historical context.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the full Arabic passage and its English translation. This will give you an overview of the five biographical entries.
Notice that each entry follows a similar pattern: lineage, key events, and death details.
2
Identify each companion's unique role
For each companion, identify a distinctive characteristic or role mentioned: poet, cunning diplomat, jurist, young governor, or first Hashimi caliph.
These roles are not exhaustive but highlight why these figures are significant.
3
Reflect on their relevance to Baqillani's argument
Consider why Baqillani might have referenced these specific individuals. Their authority and historical importance lend weight to his reasoning.
Think about how their positions (e.g., Ali's early Islam, Amr's diplomacy) connect to the doctrinal points being discussed.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) عبد الله بن رواحة بن ثعلبة بن امرىء القيس بن عمرو بن امرىء القيس الأكبر الأنصاري الخزرجي، أبو محمد أحد النقباء شهد بدراً وأحداً والخندق والحديبية وعمرة القضاء والمشاهد كلها إلا الفتح وما بعده لأنه طعن في وجهه يوم مؤتة فدلك وجهه بدمه ثم صرع بين الصفين وجعل يقول : يا معشر المسلمين ذبوا عن لحم أخيكم حتى مات، وذلك سنة ثمان للهجرة وهو شاعر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو أحد الشعراء الذين كانوا يردون عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الأذى وكان عبد الله أحد الأمراء بمؤتة وأول خارج إلى الغزو وآخر قافل.
(2) هو ابن وائل أبو عبد الله ، ويقال : أبو محمد السهمي داهية قريش ومن يضرب به المثل في الفطنة، والدهاء والحزم هاجر إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مسلماً في أوائل سنة ثمان مرافقاً الخالد بن الوليد وحاجب الكعبة عثمان بن طلحة ففرح النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقدومه هم وأسلافهم، وأمر عمراً على بعض الجيش وجهزه للغزو. قال البخاري ولاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على جيش ذات السلاسل، نزل المدينة ثم سكن مصر وبها مات.
(3) هو عبد الله بن قيس بن سليم بن حضار بن حرب صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو موسى الأشعري التميمي الفقيه المقرىء، وقد استعمله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ومعاذاً على زبيد، وعدن، وولي إمرة الكوفة لعمر، وأمره البصرة وقدم ليالي فتح خيبر وغزا وجاهد مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وحمل عنه علماً كثيراً. وقال ابن سعد حدثنا الهيثم بن عدي قال أسلم أبو موسى بمكة وهاجر إلى الحبشة، وأول مشاهدة خيبر ومات سنة اثنتين وأربعين.
(4) هو عمرو بن حزم بن زيد بن لوذان بن عمرو بن عبد عوف بن غنم بن مالك بن النجار الأنصاري الخزرجي ثم البخاري وأمه من بني ساعدة يكنى أبا الضحاك وأول مشاهده الخندق واستعمله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على أهل نجران وهم بنو الحارث بن كعب وهو ابن سبع عشرة سنة بعد أن بعث إليهم خالد بن الوليد فأسلموا، وتوفي عمرو في خلافة الخطاب بالمدينة والصحيح أنه توفي بعد الخمسين لأن محمد بن سيرين روى أنه كلم معاوية بكلام شديد لما أراد البيعة ليزيد.
(5) هو علي بن أبي طالب بن عبد المطلب بن هاشم بن عبد مناف بن قصي بن كلاب بن مرة بن كعب بن لؤي القرشي الهاشمي ابن عم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم واسم أبي طالب عبد مناف وقيل اسمه كنيته واسم هاشم عمرو وأم علي فاطمة بنت أسد بن هاشم وكنيته أبو الحسن أخو رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وصهره على ابنته فاطمة سيدة نساء العالمين وأبو السبطين وهو أول هاشمي ولد بين هاشميين وأول خليفة من بني هاشم وهو أول الناس إسلاماً في قول كثير من العلماء وهاجر إلى المدينة وشهد بدراً واحداً والخندق وبيعة الرضوان المشاهد مع رسول الله إلا تبوك فإن رسول الله خلفه على أهله وله في الجميع بلاء عظيم وأثر حسن وأعطاه اللواء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في مواطن كثيرة بيده وتوفي سنة الجحاف قتلا وكان سنه ثلاثاً وستين سنة كان على آدم مقبل العينين عظيمهما ذا بطن أصلع ربعة.
(1) Abdullah ibn Rawaha ibn Tha'laba ibn Imri' al-Qays ibn Amr ibn Imri' al-Qays al-Akbar al-Ansari al-Khazraji, Abu Muhammad, one of the chiefs. He witnessed Badr, Uhud, the Trench, Hudaybiyya, and Umrat al-Qada, and all the battles except the conquest (of Mecca) and after, because he was stabbed in his face on the day of Mu'ta, so he rubbed his face with blood, then collapsed between the ranks and kept saying: 'O Muslims, defend the flesh of your brother!' until he died. That was in the year eight of the Hijra. He was the poet of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and one of the poets who defended the Messenger of Allah from harm. He was one of the commanders at Mu'ta, the first to go out to battle and the last to return. (2) He is Ibn Wa'il, Abu Abdullah, and it is said: Abu Muhammad al-Sahmi, the cunning of Quraysh, an example in intelligence, cunning, and resolve. He migrated to the Messenger of Allah as a Muslim in early year eight, accompanying Khalid ibn al-Walid and the chamberlain of the Kaaba Uthman ibn Talha. The Prophet rejoiced at their arrival—them and their predecessors—and appointed Amr over part of the army and prepared him for battle. Al-Bukhari said: The Prophet appointed him over the army of Dhat al-Salasil. He settled in Medina, then lived in Egypt and died there. (3) He is Abdullah ibn Qays ibn Sulaym ibn Hadhar ibn Harb, the companion of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari al-Tamimi, the jurist and reciter. The Prophet appointed him and Mu'adh over Zabid and Aden, and he governed Kufa for Umar, and was appointed over Basra. He arrived on the nights of the conquest of Khaybar, fought and strove with the Prophet, and transmitted much knowledge from him. Ibn Sa'd said: al-Haytham ibn Adi narrated: Abu Musa embraced Islam in Mecca and migrated to Abyssinia, and his first battle was Khaybar. He died in the year forty-two. (4) He is Amr ibn Hazm ibn Zayd ibn Lawdhan ibn Amr ibn Abd Awf ibn Ghanm ibn Malik ibn al-Najjar al-Ansari al-Khazraji, then al-Bukhari. His mother was from Banu Sa'ida. His kunya is Abu al-Dahhak, and his first battle was the Trench. The Messenger of Allah appointed him over the people of Najran—Banu al-Harith ibn Ka'b—when he was seventeen years old, after sending Khalid ibn al-Walid to them and they became Muslim. Amr died during the caliphate of Umar in Medina, but the correct view is that he died after fifty, because Muhammad ibn Sirin narrated that he spoke harshly to Mu'awiya when he wanted the pledge of allegiance for Yazid. (5) He is Ali ibn Abi Talib ibn Abd al-Muttalib ibn Hashim ibn Abd Manaf ibn Qusayy ibn Kilab ibn Murra ibn Ka'b ibn Lu'ay al-Qurashi al-Hashimi, the cousin of the Messenger of Allah. The name of Abu Talib is Abd Manaf, and it is said that his name is his kunya. The name of Hashim is Amr. Ali's mother is Fatima bint Asad ibn Hashim. His kunya is Abu al-Hasan. He is the brother of the Messenger of Allah and his son-in-law with his daughter Fatima, the mistress of the women of the world, and the father of the two grandsons. He is the first Hashimi born between two Hashimi parents, the first caliph from Banu Hashim, and the first to embrace Islam according to many scholars. He migrated to Medina, witnessed Badr, Uhud, the Trench, and the Pledge of Ridwan, and all battles with the Messenger of Allah except Tabuk where the Prophet left him behind with his family. He performed great deeds and left a good legacy. The Messenger of Allah gave him the banner on many occasions with his own hand. He died in the year of the jahaf (great calamity) killed, and his age was sixty-three years. He was of fair complexion, with large, forward-facing eyes, a prominent belly, bald, and of medium stature.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage provides biographical entries for five companions mentioned in the main argument. Each entry includes lineage, key events, and death dates. (1) Abdullah ibn Rawaha: poet, martyr at Mu'ta. (2) Amr ibn al-As: cunning Qurayshi, early Muslim. (3) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: jurist and reciter, governor. (4) Amr ibn Hazm: governor of Najran. (5) Ali ibn Abi Talib: cousin and son-in-law of the Prophet, first caliph from Hashim. These biographies serve to identify the individuals referenced in Baqillani's refutation.

Key Terms

عمرو بن العاص
أبو موسى الأشعري
عمرو بن حزم
علي بن أبي طالب

Checkpoint
Which companion was known as the poet of the Prophet and died at the battle of Mu'ta?
A) Amr ibn al-As
B) Abdullah ibn Rawaha

Key Takeaway
These five companions—each with distinct contributions—are referenced by Baqillani to strengthen his argument through their authoritative positions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abdullah ibn Rawaha, a poet and commander, died calling others to defend his flesh. If your last words were aimed at your family or community, would they be a call to selflessness or something else? What specific step can you take today to ensure your legacy is one of sacrifice for others?
?
Amr ibn al-As was known for his cunning, but he placed it in the service of Islam. What are you most skilled at, and are you using it primarily for your own gain or for the sake of Allah? What would change if you dedicated that skill totally to Him starting tomorrow?
?
Ali ibn Abi Talib became the first Hashimi caliph and the Prophet's son-in-law, but his greatest honor was his early faith. You may have family connections or social status—do those things make you arrogant or grateful? What would it cost you to value faith over lineage and position?
