The Life and Virtues of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas
Biographical note on Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, his lineage, early Islam, and virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details and virtues of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, including his early acceptance of Islam, his status among the ten promised Paradise, and his notable deeds.

Core Idea
Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: a foremost Companion, first to shed blood for Islam, and one of the ten promised Paradise.

This passage from Imam al-Baqillani's work provides a concise biography of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, highlighting his lineage, early Islam, participation in battles, and lofty rank. Let us explore the details that illustrate his distinguished position in the early Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without focusing on translation. Let the names and details stand out.
2
Review the English translation
Compare with the translation to ensure understanding of each detail.
3
Identify key biographical points
List the key facts: his lineage, age at Islam, status among the ten promised Paradise, participation in battles, first deeds, and death details.
Notice the two different physical descriptions.
4
Reflect on his virtues
Consider what makes him notable: being among the ten promised Paradise and the first to shed blood and shoot an arrow for Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زهرة بن كلاب بن مرة بن كعب بن لؤي بن غالب بن فهر بن النضر بن كنانة القرشي الزهري يكنى أبا إسحاق أسلم بعد سنة وكان عمره لما أسلم سبع عشرة سنة . روي عنه أنه قال أسلمت قبل أن تفرض الصلاة وهو أحد الذين شهد لهم رسول الله له بالجنة وأحد العشرة سادات الصحابة وأحد الستة أصحاب الشورى الذين أخبر عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله توفي وهو عنهم راض شهد بدراً وأحداً والخندق والمشاهد كلها مع رسول الله أحد بلاء عظيماً وهو أول من أراق دماً في سبيل الله وأول من رمى بسهم في سبيل الله وتوفي سعد سنة ثمان وخمسين كان أدم طويل أفطس وقيل كان قصيراً دحداحاً غليظاً ذا هامة شتن الأصابع قالته ابنته عائشة وتوفي بالعقيق على سبعة أميال من المدينة فحمل على أعناق الرجال إلى المدينة فأدخل المسجد فصلى عليه مروان وأزواج النبي .
Zuhra bin Kilab bin Murra bin Ka'b bin Lu'ayy bin Ghalib bin Fihr bin al-Nadr bin Kinana al-Qurashi al-Zuhri, his kunya is Abu Ishaq. He accepted Islam after a year, and his age when he accepted Islam was seventeen years. It is narrated from him that he said: I accepted Islam before prayer was made obligatory. He is one of those whom the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified for Paradise, and one of the ten masters of the Companions, and one of the six members of the shura whom 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) informed that the Messenger of Allah died while being pleased with them. He witnessed Badr, Uhud, the Trench, and all the battles with the Messenger of Allah, and he performed great deeds. He was the first to shed blood in the way of Allah and the first to shoot an arrow in the way of Allah. Sa'd died in the year fifty-eight. He was tawny, tall, with a flat nose. It is also said he was short, stout, with a large head, and thick fingers. His daughter 'A'isha said that. He died in al-'Aqiq, seven miles from Medina, and was carried on the shoulders of men to Medina, and was brought into the mosque, and Marwan and the wives of the Prophet prayed over him.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (whose full name includes his lineage from Zuhra). It provides key details: his lineage tracing back to Fihr (Quraysh), his kunya Abu Ishaq, his early acceptance of Islam at age seventeen, and his claim that he accepted Islam before the five daily prayers were made obligatory. It highlights his high status as one of the ten Companions promised Paradise, one of the six members of the shura council appointed by Umar, and his participation in all major battles. It notes that he was the first to shed blood and shoot an arrow for the sake of Allah. The entry ends with his death date (58 AH) and a physical description, including conflicting reports. It also mentions details of his funeral: he died in al-'Aqiq, was carried to Medina, the mosque, and the funeral prayer was led by Marwan, with the Prophet's wives present.

Key Takeaway
Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas was a Companion of immense virtue, among the earliest Muslims, and one of the ten promised Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sa'd embraced Islam at seventeen, before prayer was made obligatory. When did you last embrace a command of Allah before it became convenient for you? What command are you still postponing?
?
Sa'd was the first to shed blood and the first to shoot an arrow for Allah's sake. Has there been a moment in your life when you were the first to stand up for the truth, even when it cost you? If not, what is holding you back from that sort of courage?
?
Sa'd was one of the ten promised Paradise—yet he still strove in battles and good deeds. If you knew with certainty that you would enter Paradise, would you still struggle to obey Allah as he did? What does your current effort reveal about your certainty?

Ali's Acceptance of the Early Caliphs: Evidence from Actions and Sayings
Lists Ali's actions and sayings showing his acceptance of the first three caliphs and includes historical narrative about Muawiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's actions and reported statements demonstrate his acceptance and respect for the first three caliphs.

Core Idea
Ali's deeds and words confirm his loyalty to Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman.

This lesson examines a passage from Imam al-Baqillani's work that compiles evidence from Ali's life to show his harmony with the early caliphs. Through specific actions like marrying his daughter to Umar and fighting alongside Abu Bakr, as well as his explicit praise, the author establishes Ali's position. We will explore these proofs and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis to get an overview. Then read the translation.
Note the structure: actions, then narrative, then sayings.
2
Identify Ali's cooperative actions
List the specific actions mentioned: submission to the three caliphs, taking spoils, marrying his daughter to Umar, carrying out a punishment in Uthman's presence, and fighting with Abu Bakr.
These actions show practical acceptance.
3
Examine the sayings
Look at the hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar being masters of Paradise's elders, and Ali's statement that he only accepted Abu Bakr's narrations without oath.
These sayings show explicit verbal respect.
4
Understand the narrative context
The passage includes a brief history of Siffin, Hasan's handover to Muawiyah, and Muawiyah's rule. This provides background but the focus remains on Ali's stance.
The 'Year of the Community' signifies unity.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Consider how this evidence counters claims of opposition among the Companions and supports Sunni views on the caliphate.
This passage is often used in sectarian discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى أن يقول بالبصرة: «بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق؟ وتعلمون أن ما ظهر منه من الانقياد لأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان والأخذ لغنيمتهم، والوطىء، وتزويجه ابنته من عمر بن الخطاب، وإقامته حداً بحضرة عثمان، وقتاله مع أبي بكر، رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، وما ثنائه عليهما، وقوله في عمر والله ما أحد ألقى الله بصحيفته كان للحنفية من سبيهم. من الطلب بدم عثمان فكان وقعة صفين بينه وبين علي وهي مشهور ثم لما قتل علي واستخلف الحسن بن علي سار معاوية إلى العراق وسار إليه الحسن بن علي فلما رأى الحسن الفتنة وأن الأمر عظيم تراق فيه الدماء ورأى اختلاف أهل العراق فسلم الأمر إلى معاوية وعاد إلى المدينة وتسلم معاوية العراق وأتى الكوفة فبايعه الناس واجتمعوا عليه فسمي عام الجماعة فبقي خليفة عشرين سنة. وكان معاوية رجلاً طويلاً أبيض جميلاً، مهيباً، وكان عمر ينظر إليه فيقول: هذا كسرى العرب. توفي معاوية النصف من رجب سنة ستين وهو ابن ثمان وسبعين سنة وقيل غير ذلك. غفلة أحبُّ إلى من هذا المسجى . وقوله في رواية سويد بن والجم الغفير من أصحابه ألا إن خير هذه الأمة بعد نبيها أبو بكر، ثم بعد أبي بكر عمر، ثم الله أعلم بالخير حيث هو، وروايته عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال لهما : هذان سيدا كهول أهل الجنة من الأولين والآخرين إلا النبيين والمرسلين، وقوله : ما حدثني أحد عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا أحلفته إلا أبا بكر ; وحدثني أبو بكر وصدق أبو بكر.
Until he said in Basra: 'They gave me allegiance in Medina and deposed me in Iraq?' And you know that what appeared from him of submission to Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and taking their spoils, and the (issue of the) slave-girl, and his marrying his daughter to Umar ibn al-Khattab, and his carrying out a legal punishment in the presence of Uthman, and his fighting alongside Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with them all, and his praise of them, and his statement regarding Umar: 'By Allah, no one will meet Allah with his record like (the one who was) from the Banu Hanifa captives?' Then from seeking vengeance for the blood of Uthman, the Battle of Siffin occurred between him (Muawiyah) and Ali, which is famous. Then when Ali was killed and al-Hasan ibn Ali became caliph, Muawiyah marched to Iraq and al-Hasan ibn Ali marched to him. When al-Hasan saw the trial and that the matter was great with bloodshed, and he saw the disagreement of the people of Iraq, he handed over the rule to Muawiyah and returned to Medina. Muawiyah took over Iraq and came to Kufa, and the people gave him allegiance and gathered around him, so it was called the Year of the Community. He remained caliph for twenty years. Muawiyah was a tall, white, handsome, majestic man. Umar used to look at him and say: 'This is the Kisra of the Arabs.' Muawiyah died in the middle of Rajab of the year sixty, and he was seventy-eight years old, and it is also said otherwise. 'Inadvertence is more beloved to me than this covered one.' And his statement in the narration of Suwayd ibn [?] and the great crowd of his companions: 'Indeed, the best of this nation after its Prophet is Abu Bakr, then after Abu Bakr is Umar, and Allah knows best where the good lies.' And his narration from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said to them: 'These two are the masters of the aged of Paradise among the first and the last, except the prophets and messengers.' And his statement: 'No one narrated to me from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) but that I made him swear, except Abu Bakr; and Abu Bakr narrated to me and Abu Bakr spoke truthfully.'
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage presents historical evidence from the words and deeds of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) to demonstrate that he accepted and was content with the caliphates of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman. The author first cites a striking phrase attributed to Ali: 'They gave me allegiance in Medina and deposed me in Iraq?' – which may refer to the events of the arbitration at Siffin. Then he lists actions that show Ali's cooperation: his submission to the first three caliphs, taking spoils from them (perhaps referring to the distribution of wealth), his marriage of his daughter Umm Kulthum to Umar, his carrying out a legal punishment in Uthman's presence, and his fighting alongside Abu Bakr against the apostates. The author then includes a narrative about the events leading to the caliphate of Muawiyah: the battle of Siffin, the assassination of Ali, and al-Hasan's peaceful transfer of power to Muawiyah in the 'Year of the Community,' along with a physical description of Muawiyah and the date of his death. Next, the author quotes sayings of Ali that extol Abu Bakr and Umar: a saying that the best of the nation after the Prophet are Abu Bakr then Umar, a hadith that the Prophet called them the masters of the aged of Paradise, and Ali's statement that he only accepted Abu Bakr's narrations without oath because he trusted him completely. These quotations serve as direct testimony from Ali that he held the first two caliphs in high esteem and acknowledged their precedence.

الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali opposed the early caliphs throughout his life.
Correction: Ali's actions and sayings show he accepted and respected Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, as documented in this passage.

Checkpoint
What action of Ali does the author cite to show his cooperation with Umar?
A) Fighting alongside Umar in battles
B) Marrying his daughter to Umar
C) Appointing Umar as his deputy
D) Giving a sermon praising Umar

Key Takeaway
Ali's actions and sayings provide clear evidence that he accepted and respected the caliphates of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ali married his daughter to Umar and fought alongside Abu Bakr—both of whom he had differences with. Is there someone in your life with whom you disagree but whom you still support in word and deed? What is holding you back from genuine unity for the sake of Allah?
?
Ali praised Abu Bakr and Umar openly, even though he might have had reservations. Think of a person you have not praised despite their good qualities. What fear or pride prevents you from acknowledging them?
?
When Hasan saw the great trial and bloodshed, he handed over rule to Muawiyah for the sake of unity. Are there conflicts in your life where you hold onto your right at the cost of community peace? What would it cost you to let go for the sake of Allah, and are you willing to pay that price?

Biography of Salim Mawla Abi Hudhayfa
Brief biography of Salim, his name, migrations, and martyrdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of the companion Salim Mawla Abi Hudhayfa, including his early Islam, migrations, and martyrdom.

Core Idea
Salim was a distinguished early companion who made two hijras and died a martyr at Yamama.

This lesson presents a concise biography of Salim, a virtuous companion of the Prophet. The passage from the text lists his merits, physical traits, and the circumstances of his martyrdom, offering a glimpse into the lives of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text along with its English translation. Pay attention to the structure and key terms.
Notice the opening word 'جمع' which indicates this is a compiled entry.
2
Identify key biographical milestones
List the major events mentioned: migrations to Abyssinia and Medina, participation in Badr, early acceptance of Islam, witnessing all campaigns, and martyrdom at Yamama.
These milestones show his dedication and high rank among companions.
3
Examine name variations and physical description
The passage gives three possible names for Salim: Muhashshim, Hushaym, and Hashim. Also note his physical traits: tall, handsome, cross-eyed, and having an extra tooth.
These details help identify him uniquely among companions.
4
Understand the mawla relationship
The text identifies him as the mawla (freed slave) of Salim, the one who was breastfed by Suhla as an adult. This refers to a well-known story about establishing mahram relations.
This connection is important for understanding his status in early Muslim society.
5
Reflect on the significance of his martyrdom
Salim was martyred at the Battle of Yamama (against Musaylima) at age 53 or 54. Consider the importance of this battle and his sacrifice.
Martyrdom is a high honor in Islam, highlighting his virtuous life.

وهاجر إلى الحبشة وإلى المدينة شهد بدراً وكان من فضلاء الصحابة الله له الشرف والفضل وكان إسلامه قبل دخول رسول الله الدار الأرقم وشهد المشاهد كلها مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقتل يوم اليمامة شهيداً وهو ابن ثلاث أو أربع وخمسين سنة وقيل اسمه مهشم وقيل هشيم وقيل هاشم وكان طويلاً حسن الوجه أحول أشعل أي له سن زائدة وهو مولى سالم الذي أرضعته زوجته سهلة كبيراً . انظر أسد الغابة ١٧٠/٥ - ١٧١ .
Collected: And he migrated to Abyssinia and to Medina, witnessed Badr, and was among the virtuous companions. God granted him honor and merit. His Islam was before the Messenger of God entered the house of al-Arqam. He witnessed all the military campaigns with the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, and was killed on the day of al-Yamama as a martyr, being three or four and fifty years old. It is said his name was Muhashshim, and it is said Hushaym, and it is said Hashim. He was tall, handsome-faced, cross-eyed, ash'al – meaning he had an extra tooth. And he is the mawla of Salim whom his wife Suhla suckled as an adult. See Usd al-Ghaba 5/170-171.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note about a companion named Salim, who is identified as Salim Mawla Abi Hudhayfa. It begins with 'jami' (collected), likely indicating a compilation entry. The biography lists his key merits: he made the two hijras (to Abyssinia and Medina), he participated in the Battle of Badr, he was among the virtuous companions, and he accepted Islam early, before the Prophet's entry into the house of al-Arqam. He attended all the military expeditions with the Prophet and was martyred at the Battle of al-Yamama against Musaylima, at the age of 53 or 54. The passage then gives variations of his name: Muhashshim, Hushaym, or Hashim. It describes his physical appearance: tall, handsome, cross-eyed (ahwal), and ash'al, meaning he had an extra tooth. Finally, it notes that he is the mawla of the well-known Salim whom Suhla breastfed as an adult (a reference to the story of Salim being nursed by Suhla to establish mahram relationship). The source is given as Usd al-Ghaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that this Salim is a different person from Salim Mawla Abi Hudhayfa, or that his name is only one form.
Correction: This Salim is the same well-known Salim Mawla Abi Hudhayfa, and the passage acknowledges multiple name variants.

Checkpoint
Which battle did Salim die in?
A) Badr
B) Uhud
C) Yamama
D) Khaybar

Key Takeaway
Salim was an early convert, made two hijras, participated in all major battles, and was martyred at Yamama at age 53/54.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Salim made two hijras, leaving behind his home and security for Allah. Is there any comfort or sin in your life that you know you must abandon but have been too attached to let go? What is one step you can take today to begin that 'hijra'?
?
Salim, a freed slave, became one of the most virtuous companions. Do you ever look down on others due to their social status, race, or past? What does Salim's story teach you about how Allah judges people?
?
Salim died a martyr at the age of 53/54, and his final years were spent in constant struggle for Allah's cause. If you were to die tonight, would you feel satisfied with how you spent your last day? What is one thing you would change?

Life of Imam al-Baqillani
beginner
6 min
Abu Bakr Leading the Prayer: A Sign of His Excellence
Baqillani presents the prayer leadership incident as proof of Abu Bakr's excellence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the event of Abu Bakr leading the prayer during the Prophet's illness to establish his superiority and refute objections.

Core Idea
Leading the Prophet in prayer was a clear designation of Abu Bakr's excellence.

Imam Baqillani begins his argument for Abu Bakr's excellence by recalling a well-known incident from the Prophet's final illness. The fact that Abu Bakr was chosen to lead the prayer, even while the Prophet was present, is presented as an undeniable sign of his rank. This lesson examines the report, the hadith cited, and Baqillani's refutation of those who try to weaken this evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of 'ضرورة' (necessarily) at the start.
2
Identify the main claim
Baqillani says Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost. Find the evidence he provides for this claim.
3
Examine the hadith
The Prophet said: 'There is no prophet who dies until a man from his people leads him in prayer.' How does Baqillani apply this to Abu Bakr?
The hadith is narrated by trustworthy narrators.
4
Consider the objection
Some opponents claim the Prophet led Abu Bakr. Baqillani dismisses this as fabrication. Why?
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that no one can be better than the Prophet while he is present, so the opponents' narrations are invalid. What does this imply?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضرورةً كما علمنا أن أبا بكر تقدم ضرورة وإنما اختلف في أن أبا بكر صلّى بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو صلّى به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة واحدة ذُكر ذلك فيها وصلّى بهم بقية أيام مرض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وروى النّبتُ الثقات أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «ما من نبي يموت حتى يؤمه رجل من قومه (۱) ؛ وأن أبا بكر أم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهذا هو الذي عناه أبو بكر بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم؛ إني وليتكم الصلاة ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاضر» (٢) ؛ ولعمري إنه لا يجوز أن يكون خير قوم فيهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا مُعْتَبر في هذا الأمر العظيم بتلفيق المخالفين وتمنيهم الأباطيل وتلقهِم بروايات ترد خاصة منهم ولهم لا يعلمها غيرهم .
هذا على أنه لو يعلم جميع من حاله، ولم يتقدم له شيء ء مما ذكرناه من فضائله ومناقبه لكان ما ظهر منه بعد موت النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من العلم والفضل والشدة في القول والفعل وتحصيل ما ذهب على غيــره دلالة على اجتماع خلال الفضل والإمامة فيه بل لو لم يدلّ على ذلك من أمره إلا ما ظهر منه من التثقيف والتقدم والتشدد وسد الخلل وقمع الرّدة وأهلها في أيام نظره لكان في ذلك مقنع لمن وُفِّقَ لرشده .
فأول ما ظهر من فضله وتسديد رأيه إعلام الناس موت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكفَّه عمر (۳) وغيره ممن تشتتت آراؤهم في موته وفجئتهم أمته عن المصيبة بموته وما كان من قوله وفعله في ذلك وقالت عائشة وغيرها من اصحابة: إن الناس أفْحِمُوا ودَهشوا حيث ارتفعت الرَّنْةُ وسَجِّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الملائكةُ بثوبه وذَهِلَ الرجال فكانوا كأجرام انتخبت منها الأرواح وحولهم أطواد من الملأ فكذب بعضهم بموته وأخرِس بعضهم فما تكلم إلا بعد الغد وخَلَّطَ آخرون ولاثوا الكلام بغير بيان وبقي آخرون معهم فكان عقولهم عمر ممن كذب بموته وعلي في من أقعاً، وعثمان في من أخرِسَ؛ وخرَجَ مَن في البيت ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مُسَجى ، وخرج عمر إلى الناس فقال عمر: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم یمت وليرجعنه الله وليقطعن أيدياً وأرجلاً من المنافقين يتمنون لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الموت وإنما واعد ربه كما واعد موسى وهو آتيكم» . وأما عليّ، فإنه قَعَدَ فلم يبرح من البيت وأما عثمان فجعل لا يكلم أحداً، يؤخذه بيده فيذهب ويُجاءُ به حتى جاء الخبر أبا بكر وتواتر أهل البيت إليه بالرسل فلقيه أحدهم بعد ما مات صلّى الله عليه وسلم وعيناه تهمُلانِ وغُصَصُه ترتفع كقطع الجرّةِ وهو في ذلك جَلْدُ العقل والمقـالـة حتى دخل على رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم فأكَبْ عليه وكشف عن وجهـه ومسحه وقبل جبينه وخديه وجعل يبكي ويقول : بأبي أنت وأمي ونفسي وأهلي، طبت حياً أحد وميتا(۲) وانقطع بموتك ما لم ينقطع بموت فعظُمَتْ من الأنبياء والنبوة الصفة المصيبة وجَلَلْت عن البكاء وخصصت حتى صرت مسلاة وعممت حتى صرنا فيك سواء ولولا أن موتك كان اختياراً منك لجدنا لموتك بالنفوس ولولا أنك نهيت عن البكاء لأنفذنا عليك ماء الشؤون . فأما ما لا تستطيع نفيه عنا فكَمَدٌ وإدناف يتحالفان لا يبرحان اللهم فأبلغه عنا : اذكرنا يا محمد عند ربك ولنكن من بالك فلولا ما خَلَّفْتَ من السكينة لم نَقُم لما خلفته من الوَحْشَةِ مِنْ اللهم ابلغ نبيك عنا واحفظه فينا»؟ ثم خرج لما قضى الناس عبراتهم وقام خطيباً فخطب فيهم خطبة جُلُّها الصلاة على النبي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Necessarily, as we know that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, and the disagreement is only whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer or the Prophet led him in one prayer, which was mentioned in that, and he led them during the remaining days of the illness of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And trustworthy narrators have narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prophet who dies until a man from his people leads him in prayer (1); and that Abu Bakr led the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in prayer.' And this is what Abu Bakr meant by his words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was present' (2). By my life, it is not permissible that the best of a people be among them while the Messenger of Allah is present. So no heed is to be paid in this great matter to the fabrications of the opponents, their wishful thinking of falsehoods, and their reception of narrations that are rejected, especially from them and to them, which none know besides them.
Moreover, if all people considered his situation, and none of his merits and virtues that we mentioned preceded, what appeared from him after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him) of knowledge, virtue, firmness in speech and action, and attainment of what escaped others would be a proof of the gathering of virtues and imamate in him. Nay, even if nothing indicated that from his affair except what appeared from him of education, precedence, strictness, filling gaps, and suppressing apostasy and its people during his days of oversight, that would be sufficient for one who is guided to his right course.
The first of his virtue and soundness of opinion that appeared was informing the people of the death of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and restraining Umar (3) and others whose opinions were scattered regarding his death and the suddenness of his nation about the calamity of his death, and what was of his saying and action in that. Aisha and others of his companions said: 'The people were struck dumb and bewildered when the wailing rose, and the angels covered the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with his garment, and men became heedless as if they were bodies from which souls had been extracted, and around them were mountains of people. Some denied his death, some were rendered speechless and did not speak until the next day, others confused and lisped without clarity, and others remained with them. Their intellects were [such that] Umar was among those who denied his death, Ali was among those who sat down, and Uthman was among those who were silenced. Those in the house left while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was covered, and Umar went out to the people and said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has not died. Allah will certainly bring him back and will cut off the hands and feet of the hypocrites who wish for the death of the Messenger of Allah. He has only made an appointment with his Lord as Moses made an appointment, and he is coming to you.' As for Ali, he sat and did not leave the house. As for Uthman, he would not speak to anyone; someone would take him by the hand and he would go and be brought back until the news reached Abu Bakr, and the people of the household sent messengers to him repeatedly. One of them met him after he (peace be upon him) had died, while his eyes were overflowing and his sobs rose like pieces of a jar, yet he was firm in mind and speech until he entered upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), bent over him, uncovered his face, wiped him, kissed his forehead and cheeks, and began to weep, saying: 'May my father, mother, soul, and family be sacrificed for you! You were good alive and dead (2). By your death, that which did not cease with the death of prophets and prophethood has ceased—the attribute of calamity. It is too great for weeping, and you are singled out until you have become a consolation, and general until we are all equal in you. Were it not that your death was a choice from you, we would have sacrificed our souls for your death. Were it not that you forbade weeping, we would have poured upon you the water of the eyes. As for what you cannot deny from us, it is grief and wasting away, which take turns and never leave. O Allah, convey from us: Remember us, O Muhammad, with your Lord, and let us be in your mind. For were it not for the tranquility you have left, we would not have stood for the loneliness you have left. O Allah, convey to your prophet from us, and protect him among us.' Then he went out when the people had finished their tears, stood as a preacher, and delivered a sermon whose most part was prayer upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument by Imam Baqillani to demonstrate the excellence of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq (RA) and his rightful claim to the caliphate. The passage can be divided into three main parts: (1) Abu Bakr's exceptional role during the Prophet's illness, (2) his virtues after the Prophet's death, and (3) a detailed narration of events immediately after the death.

First, Baqillani asserts that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, citing the well-known report that he led the prayer during the Prophet's final illness. He mentions a hadith that every prophet is led in prayer by a man from his people, and that Abu Bakr led the Prophet himself. He then quotes Abu Bakr's own words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah was present.' This shows Abu Bakr's humility and the trust placed in him. Baqillani emphatically states that it is impossible for the best of a people to be among them while the Prophet is present (since the Prophet is the best), so the opponents' objections based on fabricated narrations are invalid.

Second, Baqillani argues that even if Abu Bakr had no previous merits, his actions after the Prophet's death—his knowledge, firmness, and success in consolidating the community—are sufficient proof of his excellence and qualification for imamate. He specifically highlights Abu Bakr's role in suppressing apostasy and filling the gaps left by the Prophet's death.

Third, Baqillani provides a detailed eyewitness account of the immediate aftermath of the Prophet's death. He describes the confusion and shock among the companions: Umar denied the death, Ali sat motionless, Uthman was silent, while Abu Bakr, upon receiving the news, remained composed and went to the Prophet's body. His emotional yet controlled response—weeping, kissing the Prophet's face, and delivering a moving eulogy—demonstrates his deep love and steadfastness. He then went out and addressed the people, calming them with a sermon focused on praise of the Prophet.

Throughout, Baqillani uses this narrative to refute any doubts about Abu Bakr's superiority and right to leadership, emphasizing that his actions were guided by divine grace and sound judgment.

Key Terms
أبو بكر
الإمامة
الصلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the prayer leadership incident is insignificant or disputed beyond resolution.
Correction: Baqillani shows it is a well-established fact narrated by trustworthy sources and carries decisive weight for Abu Bakr's excellence.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what did the Prophet say about every prophet?
A) He dies until he is led in prayer by a man from his people.
B) He must be buried immediately.
C) He appoints a successor before death.
D) He always leads the prayer himself.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's appointment to lead the prayer during the Prophet's lifetime is a clear, narrated sign of his preeminence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a clear proof of someone's merit like Abu Bakr's prayer leadership, do you accept it wholeheartedly, or do you entertain doubts that align with your own biases? What would it cost you to surrender your opinions to the evidence?
?
Baqillani says it is not permissible that the best of a people be among them while the Prophet is present. How does this humility before the Prophet's status challenge your own tendency to elevate yourself or others in your community? Will you consciously practice placing the Prophet above every human relationship today?
?
The opponents are described as fabricating narrations to support their wishes. In what areas of your life do you find yourself clinging to 'wishful thinking' rather than submitting to the truth? What is one specific falsehood you need to abandon after this lesson?

Life of Imam al-Baqillani
beginner
5 min
Abu Bakr's Post-Prophetic Virtues: Proof of His Imamate
Baqillani argues that Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death prove his imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani argues that Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death—especially his knowledge, firmness, and suppression of apostasy—are sufficient proof of his imamate.

Core Idea
Post-Prophetic leadership proved Abu Bakr's virtues even if his previous merits were unknown.

Baqillani makes a powerful conditional argument: even if one ignores all of Abu Bakr's earlier merits, his conduct after the Prophet's death alone demonstrates his qualification for the caliphate. This lesson explores that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Follow the conditional argument
Baqillani says 'even if...' What is the hypothetical scenario? Notice how he sets up the argument.
The argument is structured as a reductio ad absurdum.
2
List the virtues demonstrated
Identify the qualities Baqillani attributes to Abu Bakr's post-Prophetic actions: knowledge, virtue, firmness in speech and action, and attainment of what escaped others.
3
Focus on one key achievement: suppressing apostasy
Baqillani singles out the suppression of apostasy as a sufficient proof in itself. Why is this so significant?
4
Understand the rhetorical purpose
This argument silences critics who might downplay Abu Bakr's earlier role. How does it strengthen the case for his imamate?

ضرورةً كما علمنا أن أبا بكر تقدم ضرورة وإنما اختلف في أن أبا بكر صلّى بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو صلّى به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة واحدة ذُكر ذلك فيها وصلّى بهم بقية أيام مرض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وروى النّبتُ الثقات أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «ما من نبي يموت حتى يؤمه رجل من قومه (۱) ؛ وأن أبا بكر أم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهذا هو الذي عناه أبو بكر بقوله : وليتكم ولست بخيركم؛ إني وليتكم الصلاة ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاضر» (٢) ؛ ولعمري إنه لا يجوز أن يكون خير قوم فيهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا مُعْتَبر في هذا الأمر العظيم بتلفيق المخالفين وتمنيهم الأباطيل وتلقهِم بروايات ترد خاصة منهم ولهم لا يعلمها غيرهم .
هذا على أنه لو يعلم جميع من حاله، ولم يتقدم له شيء ء مما ذكرناه من فضائله ومناقبه لكان ما ظهر منه بعد موت النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم من العلم والفضل والشدة في القول والفعل وتحصيل ما ذهب على غيــره دلالة على اجتماع خلال الفضل والإمامة فيه بل لو لم يدلّ على ذلك من أمره إلا ما ظهر منه من التثقيف والتقدم والتشدد وسد الخلل وقمع الرّدة وأهلها في أيام نظره لكان في ذلك مقنع لمن وُفِّقَ لرشده .
فأول ما ظهر من فضله وتسديد رأيه إعلام الناس موت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكفَّه عمر (۳) وغيره ممن تشتتت آراؤهم في موته وفجئتهم أمته عن المصيبة بموته وما كان من قوله وفعله في ذلك وقالت عائشة وغيرها من اصحابة: إن الناس أفْحِمُوا ودَهشوا حيث ارتفعت الرَّنْةُ وسَجِّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الملائكةُ بثوبه وذَهِلَ الرجال فكانوا كأجرام انتخبت منها الأرواح وحولهم أطواد من الملأ فكذب بعضهم بموته وأخرِس بعضهم فما تكلم إلا بعد الغد وخَلَّطَ آخرون ولاثوا الكلام بغير بيان وبقي آخرون معهم فكان عقولهم عمر ممن كذب بموته وعلي في من أقعاً، وعثمان في من أخرِسَ؛ وخرَجَ مَن في البيت ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مُسَجى ، وخرج عمر إلى الناس فقال عمر: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم یمت وليرجعنه الله وليقطعن أيدياً وأرجلاً من المنافقين يتمنون لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الموت وإنما واعد ربه كما واعد موسى وهو آتيكم» . وأما عليّ، فإنه قَعَدَ فلم يبرح من البيت وأما عثمان فجعل لا يكلم أحداً، يؤخذه بيده فيذهب ويُجاءُ به حتى جاء الخبر أبا بكر وتواتر أهل البيت إليه بالرسل فلقيه أحدهم بعد ما مات صلّى الله عليه وسلم وعيناه تهمُلانِ وغُصَصُه ترتفع كقطع الجرّةِ وهو في ذلك جَلْدُ العقل والمقـالـة حتى دخل على رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم فأكَبْ عليه وكشف عن وجهـه ومسحه وقبل جبينه وخديه وجعل يبكي ويقول : بأبي أنت وأمي ونفسي وأهلي، طبت حياً أحد وميتا(۲) وانقطع بموتك ما لم ينقطع بموت فعظُمَتْ من الأنبياء والنبوة الصفة المصيبة وجَلَلْت عن البكاء وخصصت حتى صرت مسلاة وعممت حتى صرنا فيك سواء ولولا أن موتك كان اختياراً منك لجدنا لموتك بالنفوس ولولا أنك نهيت عن البكاء لأنفذنا عليك ماء الشؤون . فأما ما لا تستطيع نفيه عنا فكَمَدٌ وإدناف يتحالفان لا يبرحان اللهم فأبلغه عنا : اذكرنا يا محمد عند ربك ولنكن من بالك فلولا ما خَلَّفْتَ من السكينة لم نَقُم لما خلفته من الوَحْشَةِ مِنْ اللهم ابلغ نبيك عنا واحفظه فينا»؟ ثم خرج لما قضى الناس عبراتهم وقام خطيباً فخطب فيهم خطبة جُلُّها الصلاة على النبي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Necessarily, as we know that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, and the disagreement is only whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer or the Prophet led him in one prayer, which was mentioned in that, and he led them during the remaining days of the illness of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And trustworthy narrators have narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prophet who dies until a man from his people leads him in prayer (1); and that Abu Bakr led the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in prayer.' And this is what Abu Bakr meant by his words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was present' (2). By my life, it is not permissible that the best of a people be among them while the Messenger of Allah is present. So no heed is to be paid in this great matter to the fabrications of the opponents, their wishful thinking of falsehoods, and their reception of narrations that are rejected, especially from them and to them, which none know besides them.
Moreover, if all people considered his situation, and none of his merits and virtues that we mentioned preceded, what appeared from him after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him) of knowledge, virtue, firmness in speech and action, and attainment of what escaped others would be a proof of the gathering of virtues and imamate in him. Nay, even if nothing indicated that from his affair except what appeared from him of education, precedence, strictness, filling gaps, and suppressing apostasy and its people during his days of oversight, that would be sufficient for one who is guided to his right course.
The first of his virtue and soundness of opinion that appeared was informing the people of the death of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and restraining Umar (3) and others whose opinions were scattered regarding his death and the suddenness of his nation about the calamity of his death, and what was of his saying and action in that. Aisha and others of his companions said: 'The people were struck dumb and bewildered when the wailing rose, and the angels covered the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with his garment, and men became heedless as if they were bodies from which souls had been extracted, and around them were mountains of people. Some denied his death, some were rendered speechless and did not speak until the next day, others confused and lisped without clarity, and others remained with them. Their intellects were [such that] Umar was among those who denied his death, Ali was among those who sat down, and Uthman was among those who were silenced. Those in the house left while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was covered, and Umar went out to the people and said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has not died. Allah will certainly bring him back and will cut off the hands and feet of the hypocrites who wish for the death of the Messenger of Allah. He has only made an appointment with his Lord as Moses made an appointment, and he is coming to you.' As for Ali, he sat and did not leave the house. As for Uthman, he would not speak to anyone; someone would take him by the hand and he would go and be brought back until the news reached Abu Bakr, and the people of the household sent messengers to him repeatedly. One of them met him after he (peace be upon him) had died, while his eyes were overflowing and his sobs rose like pieces of a jar, yet he was firm in mind and speech until he entered upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), bent over him, uncovered his face, wiped him, kissed his forehead and cheeks, and began to weep, saying: 'May my father, mother, soul, and family be sacrificed for you! You were good alive and dead (2). By your death, that which did not cease with the death of prophets and prophethood has ceased—the attribute of calamity. It is too great for weeping, and you are singled out until you have become a consolation, and general until we are all equal in you. Were it not that your death was a choice from you, we would have sacrificed our souls for your death. Were it not that you forbade weeping, we would have poured upon you the water of the eyes. As for what you cannot deny from us, it is grief and wasting away, which take turns and never leave. O Allah, convey from us: Remember us, O Muhammad, with your Lord, and let us be in your mind. For were it not for the tranquility you have left, we would not have stood for the loneliness you have left. O Allah, convey to your prophet from us, and protect him among us.' Then he went out when the people had finished their tears, stood as a preacher, and delivered a sermon whose most part was prayer upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument by Imam Baqillani to demonstrate the excellence of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq (RA) and his rightful claim to the caliphate. The passage can be divided into three main parts: (1) Abu Bakr's exceptional role during the Prophet's illness, (2) his virtues after the Prophet's death, and (3) a detailed narration of events immediately after the death.

First, Baqillani asserts that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, citing the well-known report that he led the prayer during the Prophet's final illness. He mentions a hadith that every prophet is led in prayer by a man from his people, and that Abu Bakr led the Prophet himself. He then quotes Abu Bakr's own words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah was present.' This shows Abu Bakr's humility and the trust placed in him. Baqillani emphatically states that it is impossible for the best of a people to be among them while the Prophet is present (since the Prophet is the best), so the opponents' objections based on fabricated narrations are invalid.

Second, Baqillani argues that even if Abu Bakr had no previous merits, his actions after the Prophet's death—his knowledge, firmness, and success in consolidating the community—are sufficient proof of his excellence and qualification for imamate. He specifically highlights Abu Bakr's role in suppressing apostasy and filling the gaps left by the Prophet's death.

Third, Baqillani provides a detailed eyewitness account of the immediate aftermath of the Prophet's death. He describes the confusion and shock among the companions: Umar denied the death, Ali sat motionless, Uthman was silent, while Abu Bakr, upon receiving the news, remained composed and went to the Prophet's body. His emotional yet controlled response—weeping, kissing the Prophet's face, and delivering a moving eulogy—demonstrates his deep love and steadfastness. He then went out and addressed the people, calming them with a sermon focused on praise of the Prophet.

Throughout, Baqillani uses this narrative to refute any doubts about Abu Bakr's superiority and right to leadership, emphasizing that his actions were guided by divine grace and sound judgment.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is one action of Abu Bakr that alone suffices to prove his imamate?
A) His eloquent sermon
B) Suppressing apostasy
C) Weeping at the Prophet's death
D) Leading the prayer

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's post-Prophetic leadership, especially suppressing apostasy, is clear proof of his imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you evaluate a leader, do you focus on their past credentials or their present actions? How does Baqillani’s argument challenge your tendency to overlook current proofs of virtue? Will you revise how you judge the imams of your community?
?
Abu Bakr acted with firmness and decisiveness against apostasy. In what area of your life have you been hesitant to take a clear stand for truth, fearing social backlash or personal loss? What would it mean for you to emulate his courage starting this week?
?
The passage says that even just Abu Bakr's handling of apostasy is sufficient proof of his imamate. Are there 'apostasies'—deviations from truth—in your own heart or home that you have tolerated? Will you confront them with the same seriousness?

Life of Imam al-Baqillani
beginner
8 min
The Calm After the Storm: Abu Bakr's Composure at the Prophet's Death
Baqillani narrates the events after the Prophet's death to show Abu Bakr's unique composure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will analyze the detailed narrative of the Prophet's death and see how Abu Bakr's composed response demonstrates his leadership and deep faith.

Core Idea
In the chaos of the Prophet's death, Abu Bakr's calm wisdom restored order and affirmed faith.

Baqillani provides a vivid eyewitness account of the moments after the Prophet's passing. The companions were in shock—Umar denied the death, Ali sat motionless, Uthman was speechless. Only Abu Bakr, upon arriving, showed both emotional love and steady leadership. This lesson walks through that narrative and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Set the scene
Understand the confusion among the companions. The passage describes people as 'bodies without souls'. What does this convey?
2
Note each companion's reaction
Identify how Umar, Ali, and Uthman reacted. Umar denied the death, Ali sat down, Uthman was silent.
These reactions contrast with Abu Bakr's.
3
Witness Abu Bakr's response
Abu Bakr wept, kissed the Prophet's face, and delivered a moving eulogy. How does his emotional yet controlled response show leadership?
4
Identify the lesson for imamate
Abu Bakr's composure and ability to calm others proved he was the right leader. How does this narrative serve as proof?

فأول ما ظهر من فضله وتسديد رأيه إعلام الناس موت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكفَّه عمر (۳) وغيره ممن تشتتت آراؤهم في موته وفجئتهم أمته عن المصيبة بموته وما كان من قوله وفعله في ذلك وقالت عائشة وغيرها من اصحابة: إن الناس أفْحِمُوا ودَهشوا حيث ارتفعت الرَّنْةُ وسَجِّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الملائكةُ بثوبه وذَهِلَ الرجال فكانوا كأجرام انتخبت منها الأرواح وحولهم أطواد من الملأ فكذب بعضهم بموته وأخرِس بعضهم فما تكلم إلا بعد الغد وخَلَّطَ آخرون ولاثوا الكلام بغير بيان وبقي آخرون معهم فكان عقولهم عمر ممن كذب بموته وعلي في من أقعاً، وعثمان في من أخرِسَ؛ وخرَجَ مَن في البيت ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مُسَجى ، وخرج عمر إلى الناس فقال عمر: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم یمت وليرجعنه الله وليقطعن أيدياً وأرجلاً من المنافقين يتمنون لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الموت وإنما واعد ربه كما واعد موسى وهو آتيكم» . وأما عليّ، فإنه قَعَدَ فلم يبرح من البيت وأما عثمان فجعل لا يكلم أحداً، يؤخذه بيده فيذهب ويُجاءُ به حتى جاء الخبر أبا بكر وتواتر أهل البيت إليه بالرسل فلقيه أحدهم بعد ما مات صلّى الله عليه وسلم وعيناه تهمُلانِ وغُصَصُه ترتفع كقطع الجرّةِ وهو في ذلك جَلْدُ العقل والمقـالـة حتى دخل على رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم فأكَبْ عليه وكشف عن وجهـه ومسحه وقبل جبينه وخديه وجعل يبكي ويقول : بأبي أنت وأمي ونفسي وأهلي، طبت حياً أحد وميتا(۲) وانقطع بموتك ما لم ينقطع بموت فعظُمَتْ من الأنبياء والنبوة الصفة المصيبة وجَلَلْت عن البكاء وخصصت حتى صرت مسلاة وعممت حتى صرنا فيك سواء ولولا أن موتك كان اختياراً منك لجدنا لموتك بالنفوس ولولا أنك نهيت عن البكاء لأنفذنا عليك ماء الشؤون . فأما ما لا تستطيع نفيه عنا فكَمَدٌ وإدناف يتحالفان لا يبرحان اللهم فأبلغه عنا : اذكرنا يا محمد عند ربك ولنكن من بالك فلولا ما خَلَّفْتَ من السكينة لم نَقُم لما خلفته من الوَحْشَةِ مِنْ اللهم ابلغ نبيك عنا واحفظه فينا»؟ ثم خرج لما قضى الناس عبراتهم وقام خطيباً فخطب فيهم خطبة جُلُّها الصلاة على النبي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Necessarily, as we know that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, and the disagreement is only whether Abu Bakr led the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer or the Prophet led him in one prayer, which was mentioned in that, and he led them during the remaining days of the illness of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And trustworthy narrators have narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prophet who dies until a man from his people leads him in prayer (1); and that Abu Bakr led the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in prayer.' And this is what Abu Bakr meant by his words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was present' (2). By my life, it is not permissible that the best of a people be among them while the Messenger of Allah is present. So no heed is to be paid in this great matter to the fabrications of the opponents, their wishful thinking of falsehoods, and their reception of narrations that are rejected, especially from them and to them, which none know besides them.
Moreover, if all people considered his situation, and none of his merits and virtues that we mentioned preceded, what appeared from him after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him) of knowledge, virtue, firmness in speech and action, and attainment of what escaped others would be a proof of the gathering of virtues and imamate in him. Nay, even if nothing indicated that from his affair except what appeared from him of education, precedence, strictness, filling gaps, and suppressing apostasy and its people during his days of oversight, that would be sufficient for one who is guided to his right course.
The first of his virtue and soundness of opinion that appeared was informing the people of the death of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and restraining Umar (3) and others whose opinions were scattered regarding his death and the suddenness of his nation about the calamity of his death, and what was of his saying and action in that. Aisha and others of his companions said: 'The people were struck dumb and bewildered when the wailing rose, and the angels covered the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with his garment, and men became heedless as if they were bodies from which souls had been extracted, and around them were mountains of people. Some denied his death, some were rendered speechless and did not speak until the next day, others confused and lisped without clarity, and others remained with them. Their intellects were [such that] Umar was among those who denied his death, Ali was among those who sat down, and Uthman was among those who were silenced. Those in the house left while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was covered, and Umar went out to the people and said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has not died. Allah will certainly bring him back and will cut off the hands and feet of the hypocrites who wish for the death of the Messenger of Allah. He has only made an appointment with his Lord as Moses made an appointment, and he is coming to you.' As for Ali, he sat and did not leave the house. As for Uthman, he would not speak to anyone; someone would take him by the hand and he would go and be brought back until the news reached Abu Bakr, and the people of the household sent messengers to him repeatedly. One of them met him after he (peace be upon him) had died, while his eyes were overflowing and his sobs rose like pieces of a jar, yet he was firm in mind and speech until he entered upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), bent over him, uncovered his face, wiped him, kissed his forehead and cheeks, and began to weep, saying: 'May my father, mother, soul, and family be sacrificed for you! You were good alive and dead (2). By your death, that which did not cease with the death of prophets and prophethood has ceased—the attribute of calamity. It is too great for weeping, and you are singled out until you have become a consolation, and general until we are all equal in you. Were it not that your death was a choice from you, we would have sacrificed our souls for your death. Were it not that you forbade weeping, we would have poured upon you the water of the eyes. As for what you cannot deny from us, it is grief and wasting away, which take turns and never leave. O Allah, convey from us: Remember us, O Muhammad, with your Lord, and let us be in your mind. For were it not for the tranquility you have left, we would not have stood for the loneliness you have left. O Allah, convey to your prophet from us, and protect him among us.' Then he went out when the people had finished their tears, stood as a preacher, and delivered a sermon whose most part was prayer upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument by Imam Baqillani to demonstrate the excellence of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq (RA) and his rightful claim to the caliphate. The passage can be divided into three main parts: (1) Abu Bakr's exceptional role during the Prophet's illness, (2) his virtues after the Prophet's death, and (3) a detailed narration of events immediately after the death.

First, Baqillani asserts that Abu Bakr was necessarily foremost, citing the well-known report that he led the prayer during the Prophet's final illness. He mentions a hadith that every prophet is led in prayer by a man from his people, and that Abu Bakr led the Prophet himself. He then quotes Abu Bakr's own words: 'I have been put in charge of you while I am not the best of you; indeed, I was put in charge of the prayer while the Messenger of Allah was present.' This shows Abu Bakr's humility and the trust placed in him. Baqillani emphatically states that it is impossible for the best of a people to be among them while the Prophet is present (since the Prophet is the best), so the opponents' objections based on fabricated narrations are invalid.

Second, Baqillani argues that even if Abu Bakr had no previous merits, his actions after the Prophet's death—his knowledge, firmness, and success in consolidating the community—are sufficient proof of his excellence and qualification for imamate. He specifically highlights Abu Bakr's role in suppressing apostasy and filling the gaps left by the Prophet's death.

Third, Baqillani provides a detailed eyewitness account of the immediate aftermath of the Prophet's death. He describes the confusion and shock among the companions: Umar denied the death, Ali sat motionless, Uthman was silent, while Abu Bakr, upon receiving the news, remained composed and went to the Prophet's body. His emotional yet controlled response—weeping, kissing the Prophet's face, and delivering a moving eulogy—demonstrates his deep love and steadfastness. He then went out and addressed the people, calming them with a sermon focused on praise of the Prophet.

Throughout, Baqillani uses this narrative to refute any doubts about Abu Bakr's superiority and right to leadership, emphasizing that his actions were guided by divine grace and sound judgment.

Key Terms
أبو بكر
الصديق
الفضل
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Abu Bakr's actions at the Prophet's death were merely emotional and unplanned.
Correction: Baqillani shows his actions were composed and purposeful, demonstrating leadership and sound judgment.

Checkpoint
What was Umar's initial reaction to the Prophet's death according to the passage?
A) He wept uncontrollably.
B) He denied the death and said the Prophet would return.
C) He immediately pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr.
D) He spoke to no one.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's composed and loving response to the Prophet's death demonstrates his unique qualification for leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a devastating loss, do you allow your emotions to cloud your responsibilities, or do you find strength to lead as Abu Bakr did? What would it take for you to be a source of calm for others in crisis?
?
Abu Bakr wept while remaining firm—he did not suppress his grief but channeled it. Where in your life are you suppressing emotions instead of allowing them to coexist with your duty? Will you let that change starting today?
?
If you were in the room when the Prophet (peace be upon him) died, would you have been among those who denied, remained silent, or sat still—or would you have had the composure to speak truth and lead? What would need to change in your heart now to prepare you for such a trial?

Proof 1: The Dispatch of Usama's Army
Baqillani narrates Abu Bakr's dispatch of Usama's army as the first proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's unwavering commitment to the Prophet's command regarding Usama's army demonstrated his fitness for the caliphate.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's loyalty to the Prophet's orders proved his right to lead.

Baqillani presents the first of three historical proofs of Abu Bakr's merit. He highlights Abu Bakr's refusal to alter the Prophet's appointment of Usama as commander, despite widespread opposition. This action shows Abu Bakr's deep respect for the Prophet's authority and his decisive leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Usama's army
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the context of the people's opposition and Abu Bakr's firm response.
Pay attention to Abu Bakr's physical reaction to Umar's suggestion.
2
Identify the key elements of the proof
Identify the background, the opposition, Abu Bakr's refusal, and the successful outcome. This structure shows his resolve.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why does this act prove Abu Bakr's fitness for the caliphate? Consider how it reflects his adherence to the Prophet's will.
The commentary will expand on this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى الله عليه وسلم قد مات وإني قد رأيت في وجهه ما لم أزل أعرفه في وجوه بني عبد المطلب عند الموت؛ فلم يرجعوا لقوله حتى كان من أبي بكر ما ذكرناه فرجعوا صابرين محتسبين بقوة نفس وسكون جاش في الدين ولو لم يظهر منه غير هذا الفعل لكان كافياً في العلم بفضله وما هو عليه من اجتماع ما هو مفترق في غيره. ثم شدة عقده ما كان من إنفاذه جيش أسامة ومخالفته للكافة في ترك إنفاذه مع خوفهم من الظفر من عدوهم وقولهم: إن هذا الجيش فيه الحامية من نقباء المهاجرين والأنصار وأهل الردة قد أطلعوا رؤوسهم وساقوا المدينة فانتظر بإنفاذه انكشاف الردة، فقال: والله لأن أخر من السماء فتخطفني الطير وتنهشني السباع أحب إلي من أن أكون أول حال لعقد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنفذوا جيش أسامة. ونادى مناديه بخروجهم وسأل نقباء المهاجرين والأنصار عمر أن يسأل أبا بكر أن يصرف أسامة ويولي من هو أسن وأدرب بالحرب منه فسأله عمر ذلك فوثب إليه وأخذ لحيته بيده فهزها وقال: ثكلتك أمك يا ابن الخطاب وعدمتك أيوليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وتأمرني أن أصرفه؟ والله لا يكون ذلك أبدا؛ فأمرهم بالخروج وشيعهم أبو بكر حافيا والعباس معه ومن بقي من الصحابة في المدينة فما زال يدعو لهم ويأمر العباس بالتأمين على دعائه، وأسامة يقول: إما أن تركب يا خليفة رسول الله أو أنزل، وهو يقول: لا والله لا أركب ولا تنزل وماذا علي أن تغبر قدماي في تشييع غاز في سبيل الله تعالى. فنفذ الجيش وفتح الله لهم وغنم ورجع في نيف وستين يوما ولقي بهم أهل الردة. ثم ما كان منه في قتال أهل الردة وسدة ثلم المدينة وخروجه لمناضلتهم بنفسه ومن معه حتى دفعهم قبل عود جيش أسامة، وندائه في المدينة ألا أحد أحدا من رسل أهل الردة لما وفدوا إليه الوفود يسألونه الصلح على ترك الزكاة وقوله لما سألوه رفع السيف عنهم وأذعنوا بأداء الزكاة: لا والله أو يقولوا إن قتلاهم في النار وقتلانا في الجنة، ثم إنفاذه خالد بن الوليد ومن معه من الجيوش إلى أهل الردة ومسيلمة ومن باليمامة من دعاة الكفر حتى أبادهم واستأصل خضراءهم وأيد الله به الدين وكشف العمة وأزال الكربة ورد الحق إلى نصابه وانحسرت بيمنه الفتنة وضعفت منهة أهل الكفر وفشلوا قبل لقاء عسكره حتى قال قائلهم المشهور شعره: ألا عللاني قبل جيش أبي بكر لعل منايانا قريب وما ندري لعل جيوش المسلمين وخالدا سيطرقنا قبل الصباح من البر فصبحتهم الخيل. قال الراوي: فكان رأس هذا الشاعر أول رأس رمي به تداكد في باطئة الجمر. فكيف لا يصلح من هذه صفته لإمامة الأمة؟
May God bless him and grant him peace had died, and I have seen in his face what I have always known in the faces of the Banu Abd al-Muttalib at death; so they did not retract from his statement until what we mentioned from Abu Bakr happened, so they retracted, patient, seeking reward, with strength of soul and calmness of heart in the religion. Even if nothing else had appeared from him except this act, it would have been sufficient for knowing his virtue and his state of combining what is scattered in others. Then the severity of his determination was what happened from his dispatch of the army of Usama and his opposition to all [others] in leaving its dispatch, despite their fear of defeat from their enemy and their saying: 'This army contains the protectors from the notables of the Muhajirun and Ansar, and the people of apostasy have raised their heads and besieged Medina, so wait with its dispatch for the uncovering of the apostasy.' He said: 'By God, if I were to fall from the sky and be snatched by birds and bitten by beasts, that would be more beloved to me than to be the first to undo a knot tied by the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. Dispatch the army of Usama.' And his herald announced their departure. The notables of the Muhajirun and Ansar asked Umar to ask Abu Bakr to divert Usama and appoint someone older and more experienced in war. Umar asked him that, and he [Abu Bakr] leaped at him, took his beard in his hand, shook it, and said: 'May your mother lose you, O son of al-Khattab, and may you be bereft! Will the Messenger of God appoint him and you order me to divert him? By God, that will never be.' So he ordered them to depart, and Abu Bakr saw them off barefoot, with al-Abbas and the remaining Companions in Medina. He kept supplicating for them and ordered al-Abbas to say 'Amin' to his supplication. Usama said: 'Either you ride, O Caliph of the Messenger of God, or I will dismount.' And he said: 'No, by God, I will not ride, and you will not dismount. What does it matter to me if my feet become dusty in seeing off a warrior in the path of God Almighty?' So the army set out, and God granted them victory and spoils, and they returned in about sixty days, and they met the apostates. Then what he did in fighting the apostates and closing the breach of Medina, and his going out to fight them with himself and those with him until he repelled them before the return of Usama's army; and his proclamation in Medina: 'Let no one [receive] any messenger from the apostates!' when delegations came to him asking for peace on condition of abandoning zakat, and his saying when they asked him to lift the sword from them if they submitted to paying zakat: 'No, by God, or they say that their dead are in the Fire and our dead are in Paradise.' Then his dispatch of Khalid ibn al-Walid and the armies with him against the apostates, Musaylima, and those in al-Yamama from the callers to unbelief, until he destroyed them and eradicated them completely, and God strengthened the religion through him, and removed the affliction and distress, and restored the truth to its rightful place, and tribulation receded through his blessing, and the strength of the people of unbelief weakened, and they failed even before meeting his army, so much so that their famous reciter said in his poetry: 'Alas, both of you, refresh me before the army of Abu Bakr, for perhaps our deaths are near and we do not know; perhaps the armies of the Muslims and Khalid will strike us before dawn in the land.' And the cavalry attacked them at morning. The narrator said: 'The head of this reciter was the first head thrown, rolling in the hollow of the embers.' So how could one with these attributes not be fit for the imamate of the community?
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument by Baqillani demonstrating the worthiness of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (RA) for the caliphate. The author presents three distinct actions of Abu Bakr that prove his excellence and right to leadership. The passage begins with a prior incident where the people finally accepted Abu Bakr's view after the Prophet's death, noting that even this alone would have been enough to show his virtue. Then the first major proof: Abu Bakr's insistence on dispatching Usama's army despite widespread opposition and fear. He refused to cancel or delay a command of the Prophet, and when Umar suggested replacing Usama with an older commander, Abu Bakr reacted forcefully, grabbing Umar's beard and swearing he would never alter the Prophet's appointment. He personally saw the army off barefoot. The second proof: during the Ridda wars, Abu Bakr personally fought the apostates and closed the breach in Medina. When delegations sought peace by withholding zakat, Abu Bakr refused absolutely, demanding that they accept zakat or face war, stating that they must acknowledge that their dead are in the Fire and the Muslims' dead in Paradise. The third proof: Abu Bakr sent Khalid ibn al-Walid with armies against the apostates and Musaylima, achieving a complete victory that strengthened Islam and ended the threat. The author quotes a verse from an enemy poet expressing fear before Abu Bakr's army, and an anecdote about the poet's head being the first thrown. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: 'So how could one with these attributes not be fit for the imamate of the community?' Thus, each action reinforces the argument that Abu Bakr's firmness, loyalty to the Prophet's commands, and successful leadership make him the rightful caliph.

Key Terms
جيش أسامة
خلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Bakr refuse to replace Usama as the commander of the army?
A) He thought Usama was more experienced in war.
B) He did not want to oppose the Prophet's appointment.
C) He feared the army would not follow a new commander.
D) He wanted to appoint himself as commander.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's refusal to alter the Prophet's appointment demonstrated his absolute fidelity to the Sunna, qualifying him for the caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Bakr said he would rather die than undo a knot tied by the Messenger of God. What 'knot' has Allah tied in your life—a command, a duty, a relationship—that you are tempted to loosen or ignore because of others' opinions? What would it cost you to obey it fully?
?
When Umar suggested a practical alternative, Abu Bakr's response was fierce and immediate. Have you ever faced a situation where human wisdom contradicted a clear command from Allah? Which did you choose, and what did that choice reveal about your heart?
?
Abu Bakr walked barefoot to see off the army, humbling himself for the sake of Allah's cause. What act of humility is Allah calling you to perform today that you have been avoiding because it would lower your status in people's eyes?

Proof 2: Fighting the Apostates and Defending Zakat
Baqillani narrates Abu Bakr's fight against apostates and defence of zakat as the second proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's personal courage and uncompromising stance on zakat during the Ridda wars proved his fitness for the caliphate.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr defended the pillars of Islam with unwavering resolve.

The second proof focuses on Abu Bakr's actions during the apostasy wars. He personally fought to close the breach in Medina and refused to compromise on zakat, a fundamental obligation of Islam. This demonstration of firmness in religious matters further supports his right to lead.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Ridda wars
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two aspects: personal fighting and the zakat refusal.
Look for the phrase 'لا والله أو يقولوا...'
2
Identify the actions of Abu Bakr
List his actions: going out to fight, proclaiming against apostate messengers, and rejecting peace without zakat.
3
Consider the significance
Why are these acts proof of his leadership? Reflect on how he protected the religion and enforced its obligations.
This shows his commitment to upholding Islamic law.

Checkpoint
What condition did the apostate delegations propose for peace?
A) They would pay zakat but not pray.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you compromised on a religious obligation to make peace with someone? What would it cost you to stand firm like Abu Bakr?
?
Abu Bakr declared that those who abandon zakat are in the Fire. How does that certainty affect your own commitment to fulfilling obligations you find difficult?
?
If you were in Abu Bakr's position, facing delegations who offered partial submission, would you have the courage to reject them outright — knowing it means war? What holds you back from such resolve?

Proof 3: Defeating Musaylima and the Apostates
Baqillani narrates Abu Bakr's dispatch of Khalid ibn al-Walid as the third proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's decisive dispatch of Khalid ibn al-Walid to defeat the major apostate movements confirmed his fitness to lead the Muslim community.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's strategic leadership crushed the apostasy and restored Islamic order.

The third proof showcases Abu Bakr's strategic acumen. He sent Khalid ibn al-Walid with powerful armies against the strongest apostate forces, including Musaylima. The complete victory not only eliminated the threat but also strengthened Islam. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question affirming his right to the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Khalid's campaign
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the description of the victory and the enemy's fear.
Note the poetic verse quoted from the enemy.
2
Identify the outcomes of the campaign
List the results: eradication of apostates, strengthening of religion, removal of affliction, and restoration of truth.
3
Analyze the rhetorical question
Consider why Baqillani ends with 'How could one with these attributes not be fit for the imamate?' This ties the proofs together.
This is the conclusion of the entire argument.

سبيل الله تعالى. فنفذ الجيش وفتح الله لهم وغنم ورجع في نيف وستين يوما ولقي بهم أهل الردة. ثم ما كان منه في قتال أهل الردة وسدة ثلم المدينة وخروجه لمناضلتهم بنفسه ومن معه حتى دفعهم قبل عود جيش أسامة، وندائه في المدينة ألا أحد أحدا من رسل أهل الردة لما وفدوا إليه الوفود يسألونه الصلح على ترك الزكاة وقوله لما سألوه رفع السيف عنهم وأذعنوا بأداء الزكاة: لا والله أو يقولوا إن قتلاهم في النار وقتلانا في الجنة، ثم إنفاذه خالد بن الوليد ومن معه من الجيوش إلى أهل الردة ومسيلمة ومن باليمامة من دعاة الكفر حتى أبادهم واستأصل خضراءهم وأيد الله به الدين وكشف العمة وأزال الكربة ورد الحق إلى نصابه وانحسرت الخيل. قال الراوي: فكان رأس هذا الشاعر أول رأس رمي به تداكد في باطئة الجمر. فكيف لا يصلح من هذه صفته لإمامة الأمة؟
May God bless him and grant him peace had died, and I have seen in his face what I have always known in the faces of the Banu Abd al-Muttalib at death; so they did not retract from his statement until what we mentioned from Abu Bakr happened, so they retracted, patient, seeking reward, with strength of soul and calmness of heart in the religion. Even if nothing else had appeared from him except this act, it would have been sufficient for knowing his virtue and his state of combining what is scattered in others. Then the severity of his determination was what happened from his dispatch of the army of Usama and his opposition to all [others] in leaving its dispatch, despite their fear of defeat from their enemy and their saying: 'This army contains the protectors from the notables of the Muhajirun and Ansar, and the people of apostasy have raised their heads and besieged Medina, so wait with its dispatch for the uncovering of the apostasy.' He said: 'By God, if I were to fall from the sky and be snatched by birds and bitten by beasts, that would be more beloved to me than to be the first to undo a knot tied by the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. Dispatch the army of Usama.' And his herald announced their departure. The notables of the Muhajirun and Ansar asked Umar to ask Abu Bakr to divert Usama and appoint someone older and more experienced in war. Umar asked him that, and he [Abu Bakr] leaped at him, took his beard in his hand, shook it, and said: 'May your mother lose you, O son of al-Khattab, and may you be bereft! Will the Messenger of God appoint him and you order me to divert him? By God, that will never be.' So he ordered them to depart, and Abu Bakr saw them off barefoot, with al-Abbas and the remaining Companions in Medina. He kept supplicating for them and ordered al-Abbas to say 'Amin' to his supplication. Usama said: 'Either you ride, O Caliph of the Messenger of God, or I will dismount.' And he said: 'No, by God, I will not ride, and you will not dismount. What does it matter to me if my feet become dusty in seeing off a warrior in the path of God Almighty?' So the army set out, and God granted them victory and spoils, and they returned in about sixty days, and they met the apostates. Then what he did in fighting the apostates and closing the breach of Medina, and his going out to fight them with himself and those with him until he repelled them before the return of Usama's army; and his proclamation in Medina: 'Let no one [receive] any messenger from the apostates!' when delegations came to him asking for peace on condition of abandoning zakat, and his saying when they asked him to lift the sword from them if they submitted to paying zakat: 'No, by God, or they say that their dead are in the Fire and our dead are in Paradise.' Then his dispatch of Khalid ibn al-Walid and the armies with him against the apostates, Musaylima, and those in al-Yamama from the callers to unbelief, until he destroyed them and eradicated them completely, and God strengthened the religion through him, and removed the affliction and distress, and restored the truth to its rightful place, and tribulation receded through his blessing, and the strength of the people of unbelief weakened, and they failed even before meeting his army, so much so that their famous reciter said in his poetry: 'Alas, both of you, refresh me before the army of Abu Bakr, for perhaps our deaths are near and we do not know; perhaps the armies of the Muslims and Khalid will strike us before dawn in the land.' And the cavalry attacked them at morning. The narrator said: 'The head of this reciter was the first head thrown, rolling in the hollow of the embers.' So how could one with these attributes not be fit for the imamate of the community?
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is a historical argument by Baqillani demonstrating the worthiness of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (RA) for the caliphate. The author presents three distinct actions of Abu Bakr that prove his excellence and right to leadership. The passage begins with a prior incident where the people finally accepted Abu Bakr's view after the Prophet's death, noting that even this alone would have been enough to show his virtue. Then the first major proof: Abu Bakr's insistence on dispatching Usama's army despite widespread opposition and fear. He refused to cancel or delay a command of the Prophet, and when Umar suggested replacing Usama with an older commander, Abu Bakr reacted forcefully, grabbing Umar's beard and swearing he would never alter the Prophet's appointment. He personally saw the army off barefoot. The second proof: during the Ridda wars, Abu Bakr personally fought the apostates and closed the breach in Medina. When delegations sought peace by withholding zakat, Abu Bakr refused absolutely, demanding that they accept zakat or face war, stating that they must acknowledge that their dead are in the Fire and the Muslims' dead in Paradise. The third proof: Abu Bakr sent Khalid ibn al-Walid with armies against the apostates and Musaylima, achieving a complete victory that strengthened Islam and ended the threat. The author quotes a verse from an enemy poet expressing fear before Abu Bakr's army, and an anecdote about the poet's head being the first thrown. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: 'So how could one with these attributes not be fit for the imamate of the community?' Thus, each action reinforces the argument that Abu Bakr's firmness, loyalty to the Prophet's commands, and successful leadership make him the rightful caliph.

مسيلمة

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's decisive victory through Khalid ibn al-Walid proved his ability to protect and strengthen the Muslim community, confirming his right to the caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a crisis in your life, do you act with the decisive resolve of Abu Bakr, or do you delay and make excuses? What is one step you can take today to overcome hesitation in fulfilling your responsibilities?
?
The enemies of truth were terrified before the battle even began. Is there a fear in your heart that prevents you from standing for truth? What is it, and how can you trust in Allah's support as Abu Bakr did?
?
Abu Bakr's actions restored the truth to its rightful place. In your own sphere of influence, where has the truth been displaced due to your neglect or compromise? What will you commit to restore today?

Abu Bakr's Campaigns Against the Apostates
Baqillani recounts Abu Bakr's military actions against the apostates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events and firm stance of Abu Bakr in suppressing the apostasy movement after the Prophet's death.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's leadership preserved the ummah through decisive action against apostasy.

After the Prophet's death, many tribes abandoned Islam or refused zakah. Abu Bakr's unwavering response, both personally and through his generals like Khalid ibn al-Walid, solidified the early Islamic state. This passage recounts his military campaigns and his firm condition for peace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequence of events: Usama's expedition, defense of Medina, refusal to compromise on zakah, dispatch of Khalid.
2
Identify Abu Bakr's key actions
List the specific actions Abu Bakr took: personally defending Medina, proclaiming no compromise on zakah, sending Khalid to eliminate Musaylimah. Consider what each action reveals about his leadership.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this narrative is important for establishing Abu Bakr's qualifications for the imamate. How does it demonstrate his courage, adherence to Islamic law, and effectiveness as a leader?
This connects to the broader theme of defending the faith.
