So the army marched and Allah granted them victory, they took spoils and returned in a little over sixty days, and they met the people of apostasy. Then what he did in fighting the people of apostasy, repairing the breach of Medina, and going out to fight them himself with those with him until he repelled them before the return of Usama's army; and his proclamation in Medina: 'Let none of the messengers of the apostates come to me!' when delegations came to him asking for peace on condition of leaving off zakah, and his saying when they asked him to lift the sword from them and they would pay zakah: 'No, by Allah, until they say that their dead are in the Fire and our dead are in Paradise.' Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative presenting Abu Bakr's decisive actions against the apostates after the Prophet's death. It begins with the expedition of Usama, then describes Abu Bakr's personal role in defending Medina, his firm refusal to compromise on zakah, and his dispatch of Khalid to eliminate the false prophet Musaylimah. The poet's verse and its outcome dramatize the enemy's fear. The author uses this account to demonstrate Abu Bakr's courage, leadership, and unwavering commitment to Islamic law, thereby establishing his credentials for the imamate.

Umar's Consultation and Prophetic Praises
Baqillani enumerates prophetic hadiths about Umar's virtue and his consultative practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic hadiths establish Umar's high station and his consultative leadership style as evidence for his suitability for the caliphate.

Core Idea
Prophetic hadiths affirm Umar's unique status and his role as a fortress of Islam.

Baqillani begins by acknowledging that Umar consulted others, but then shows that even greater proof lies in the Prophet's own words. The hadiths cited here highlight Umar's awe-inspiring presence, his closeness to truth, and his role in strengthening Islam. Let's examine these statements that elevate Umar above ordinary companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial statement on consultation
Notice how Baqillani acknowledges Umar's reliance on Ali and Muadh while emphasizing his own knowledge and consultative method.
This sets up the argument that consultation is a virtue, not a weakness.
2
Identify the prophetic hadiths
Find each hadith: the story of the wives, the 'if not sent' hadith, the 'truth on tongue' hadith, the 'inspired ones' hadith, the 'lock of Islam' hadith, and the prayer for Umar or Abu Jahl.
These hadiths are quoted to demonstrate divine endorsement of Umar.
3
Analyze the effect of these hadiths
Ask: How do these hadiths collectively portray Umar? They show his authority, truthfulness, and central role in early Islam.
The hadiths build a cumulative case for Umar's exceptional status.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical purpose
Consider that Baqillani uses these hadiths to prove Umar is not just any companion but divinely chosen for leadership.
This sets the stage for the final conclusion in the next lesson.

In our opinion. And he says: 'If not for Ali, Umar would have been lost, and if not for Muadh, Umar would have perished (2). He does not execute judgments except with the assembly of his companions, their presence, and consultation with them, despite his merit, jurisprudence, and good insight into the sources of rulings, the methods of analogy, and knowledge of traditions. And if that had not appeared from his actions and were not known from his inner state and character, it would suffice in his regard and the knowledge of his merit and precedence what has been narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, concerning him, such as his saying: when he sought permission to enter upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and there was a group of his wives and others, and their voices had become loud in addressing the Prophet until Umar sought permission and they recognized his voice, they hastened to the veil. When he entered upon the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, he laughed; so Umar said to him: 'What makes you smile? May Allah make your teeth smile (i.e., may He make you happy).' The Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said to him: 'I marvel at these women who were laughing, and when they heard your voice, they hastened to the veil.' So Umar turned his face toward the house in which they were and said: 'O enemies of themselves! You fear me but do not fear the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace? By Allah, he is more deserving that you fear him.' The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Do not blame them, O Umar, and be gentle with them, for by Allah, you never entered a mountain pass but that Satan entered a pass other than your pass, O Umar (3).' And his saying: 'If I were not sent among you, Umar would have been sent' ( ) ( ) 'And if there were to be a prophet after me, it would be Umar (*)' 'And indeed Allah has placed the truth on the tongue of Umar and his heart (6); he speaks the truth even if it is bitter.' And his saying: 'Among you are those who speak with inspiration (muhaddathun) and those who debate; and Umar is among them (7).' And his saying: 'Umar is the lock of Islam.' And his saying: 'O Allah, strengthen Islam and support this religion with one of these two men: Umar ibn al-Khattab or Abu Jahl ibn Hisham (1).' So the supplication preceded (applied to) Umar, and Allah manifested the religion and strengthened the believers through him. And his saying: 'Allah will not be worshipped in secret after this day.' And he used to say to the people of Mecca at that time: 'By Allah, if our number reaches one hundred, you will certainly leave it for us, or we will leave it for you (2).' Meaning that he was raising the banner of war in Mecca and fighting them for the establishment of truth. And to recount his virtues and merits and the comprehensive statements of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, concerning him, and the statements of the Companions such as their saying: 'By Allah, Umar was for Islam a strong fortress: people entered it and did not leave it. When he died, that fortress was breached and collapsed (3).' 'By Allah, we did not pray openly until Umar accepted Islam ( ),' and similar examples of what they said in poetry and prose, which is lengthy and abundant. So it is clear from this summary that he is of the description of one to whom the delegation (al-'ahd) is suitable, and the initiation of the contract (al-'aqd) for him, and above the description of imamate that the contractors seek and aim for.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative proof of Umar ibn al-Khattab's suitability for the caliphate, presented by Baqillani. It begins with a statement: 'In our opinion. And he says: “If not for Ali, Umar would have been lost, and if not for Muadh, Umar would have perished.” This acknowledges Umar’s reliance on other Companions for knowledge, but immediately followed by noting that Umar did not execute judgments except after consulting with his companions, despite his own extensive knowledge of jurisprudence, analogy, and traditions. The author then argues that even if these actions were not visible, the numerous hadith from the Prophet and statements of the Companions would suffice to establish Umar’s virtue and precedence. He then lists several hadith: (1) The story of Umar’s visit to the Prophet’s wives: when they heard Umar’s voice, they veiled out of awe, and the Prophet praised Umar’s awe-inspiring presence, noting that Satan avoids Umar. (2) The hadith: 'If I were not sent among you, Umar would be sent' and 'If there were to be a prophet after me, it would be Umar.' (3) 'Allah has placed the truth on Umar’s tongue and heart.' (4) 'Among you are those who speak with divine inspiration, and Umar is one of them.' (5) 'Umar is the lock of Islam.' (6) The Prophet’s prayer to strengthen Islam with either Umar or Abu Jahl, and it was fulfilled with Umar. (7) 'Allah will not be worshipped in secret after this day'—indicating Umar’s role in enabling open worship. (8) Umar’s own threat to the polytheists. Then the author mentions that reciting all of Umar’s virtues and statements of the Prophet and Companions would be lengthy, giving examples: the Companions called him a fortress through which people entered Islam and not leave, and they said they did not pray openly until Umar embraced Islam. The passage concludes that from all this evidence it is clear that Umar is of the description suitable for delegation (al-'ahd) and initiation of the contract for him, and even surpasses the level of imamate that the contractors seek. The structure is: first, acknowledgment of Umar’s consultative method; second, appeal to prophetic hadith establishing his high status; third, companion testimonies; fourth, conclusion of his qualification.

Key Terms
العهد (al-'ahd): delegation or appointment
العقد (al-'aqd): contract of allegiance
الإمامة (al-imamah): leadership
المحدثون (al-muhaddathun): those inspired by Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's reliance on Ali and Muadh indicates he lacked knowledge or competence for the caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani shows that despite his knowledge, Umar consulted others—a virtue, not a flaw—and the prophetic hadiths affirm his exceptional status.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith about the wives, what did the Prophet say about Umar and Satan?
A) Satan often accompanies Umar
B) Satan avoids the path Umar takes
C) Satan inspires Umar
D) Satan is afraid of Umar

Key Takeaway
Prophetic hadiths collectively establish Umar's unique status and divine selection for leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said that Satan avoids Umar's path. Do you consider yourself a person whose presence makes others more conscious of Allah, or do you blend in with the environment? What steps will you take this week to become someone who drives away whispers of evil by your very character?
?
Umar spoke the truth even when it was bitter. Is there a truth you have been avoiding speaking for fear of backlash or discomfort? Will you commit to speaking it with wisdom and courage before the end of this week?
?
The Prophet's prayer for Umar transformed him from a potential enemy into the lock of Islam. What is one prayer you need to make for yourself or someone else, trusting that Allah can change a person completely? How will you act on that prayer starting today?

Companion Testimonies and Umar's Qualification for the Caliphate
Baqillani presents companion testimonies and concludes Umar's qualification for the caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how companion statements confirm Umar's suitability for the caliphate and why Baqillani concludes that Umar exceeds the standard requirements for imamate.

Core Idea
Companion testimonies and prophetic hadiths converge to prove Umar's unique qualification for the caliphate.

After presenting prophetic hadiths, Baqillani turns to the statements of the Companions, who describe Umar as a fortress of Islam and credit his conversion with enabling open prayer. These testimonies, along with the earlier hadiths, lead to the conclusion that Umar is not only fit for the caliphate but exceeds its requirements.

Guided Path
1
Read the companion statements
Identify the two key statements: 'Umar was a strong fortress for Islam' and 'we did not pray openly until he embraced Islam.'
These statements come from respected Companions and carry weight.
2
Analyze the fortress metaphor
The fortress imagery emphasizes that Umar's leadership protected and stabilized the Muslim community.
This metaphor implies strength, security, and permanence.
3
Examine Baqillani's conclusion
Read the final sentence: Umar is suitable for delegation and contract, and above the description of imamate.
This is the culmination of the entire argument.
4
Reflect on the cumulative evidence
Consider how the hadiths and companion statements together build an undeniable case for Umar's caliphal qualification.
Baqillani uses a 'weight of evidence' approach.

In our opinion. And he says: 'If not for Ali, Umar would have been lost, and if not for Muadh, Umar would have perished (2). He does not execute judgments except with the assembly of his companions, their presence, and consultation with them, despite his merit, jurisprudence, and good insight into the sources of rulings, the methods of analogy, and knowledge of traditions. Defending Uthman: The Story of Abu Dharr
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman banished Abu Dharr unjustly by providing alternative narrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends Uthman against the accusation of unjustly banishing Abu Dharr by presenting alternative narrations from reliable sources.

Core Idea
Historical accusations must be weighed against reliable narrations, not sectarian bias.

The story of Abu Dharr and Uthman has been used by some to criticize the third caliph. Baqillani tackles this head-on, not by dismissing the events, but by presenting counter-narratives from trusted scholars that paint a different picture. This lesson examines his argument and the sources he relies on.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full argument. Notice the shift from the accusation to Baqillani's commentary and then to the alternative narrations.
2
Identify the accusation and Baqillani's response
Find where Baqillani describes what the critics claim about Uthman and Abu Dharr, and note how he immediately questions the validity of the story.
He says 'كل هذا يحق لو ثبت إبعاده على هذا الوجه فكيف ولم يثبت؟'
3
Compare the two counter-narrations
Baqillani presents two narrations from Muhammad ibn Sirin and Qatada. Compare them: how does each one exonerate Uthman?
Both show that Abu Dharr chose to leave, not that he was banished.
4
Reflect on the methodological point
Notice that Baqillani contrasts the narrations of 'Ahl al-Sunnah' with those of 'the people of innovation' (Rawafid). This highlights the importance of relying on trustworthy narrators in historical debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يطعن على عثمان وعلى أمرائه ويقول إنهم قد استأثروا بالمال وعلوا البنيان وركبوا المراكب وكان هذا عنده منكراً رحمه الله لأنه كان ممن يزهد في الدنيا ويرغب في الآخرة ويرى أن التمتع بزينة الدنيا حرام وليس كما توهم. وذُكِرَ أنه أفسد على عثمان الشام وكان أبداً يقول إذا دخل على خلفائه : يوم عليها في نار جهنم فتكوى بها جباههم وجنوبهم وظهورهم هذا ما كنزتم لأنفسكم فذوقوا ما كنتم تكنزون؛ ويغرق في مجاهرتهم بأغلظ القول وليس له فعل هذا فأنكر عليه ذلك عثمان وقال له : إما أن تقيم وتكف عما يثير الفتنة أو تبعد إلى حيث لا يسمع منك ولا ينكر فعلك وكل هذا يحق لو ثبت إبعاده على هذا الوجه فكيف ولم يثبت؟ وإنما اختار الخروج إلى الربذة. ولما قدم إليها كان لعثمان غلام يصلي بالناس فقدم أبا ذر للصلاة فقال له : أنت الوالي، والوالي أحق. وهذا كله على تقدير صحة ما نقله الروافض في قصة أبي ذر مع عثمان ؛ وإلا فقد روى محمد بن سيرين خلاف ذلك فقال : لما قدم أبو ذر الشام استأذن عثمان في لحوقه بالربذة فقال عثمان : أقم عندي تغدو عليك اللقاح وتروح فقال : لا حاجة لي في الدنيا، فأذن له في الخروج إلى الربذة . وروى قتادة : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لأبي ذر إذا رأيت المدينة بلغ بناؤها سلعا فاخرج منها وأشار إلى الشام فلما كان في ولاية عثمان بلغ بناؤها سلعا فخرج إلى الشام، وأنكر على معاوية أشياء فشكاه إلى عثمان، فكتب عثمان إلى أبي ذر أقبل إلينا فنحن أرعى لحقك وأحسن جواراً من معاوية فقال أبو ذر : سمعاً وطاعة فقدم على عثمان ثم استأذن في الخروج إلى الربذة فأذن له فمات. ورواية هذين الإمامين العالمين - محمد بن سيرين وقتادة - من التابعين وأهل السنة هذه القصة أشبه بأبي ذر وعثمان من رواية غيرهما من أهل البدعة.
He attacks Uthman and his governors, saying that they have taken sole possession of wealth, built tall buildings, and ridden mounts, and this was to him objectionable, may Allah have mercy on him, because he was one of those who abstain from this world and desire the afterlife, and he considered enjoyment of the adornment of this world forbidden and it is not as they imagined. And it was mentioned that he corrupted Syria for Uthman, and he would always say when he entered upon his caliphs: The day will come upon them in the fire of Hell, and it will brand their foreheads, sides, and backs: This is what you hoarded for yourselves, so taste what you used to hoard; and he would go to extremes in confronting them with the harshest speech, though it was not for him to do this. So Uthman disapproved of that and said to him: Either you stay and refrain from what stirs up discord, or you go away to where your words cannot be heard and your action is not disapproved. And all this would be justified if his banishment were proven in this manner, but how can it be when it is not proven? Rather, he chose to go out to al-Rabdhah. And when he came to it, Uthman had a slave leading the people in prayer, so he put Abu Dharr forward for prayer and said to him: You are the governor, and the governor has more right. And all this on the assumption of the authenticity of what the Rawafid related about the story of Abu Dharr with Uthman; otherwise, Muhammad ibn Sirin narrated contrary to that, saying: When Abu Dharr came to Syria, he asked Uthman's permission to go to al-Rabdhah, and Uthman said: Stay with me; the milch camels will come to you morning and evening. He said: I have no need of the world. So he permitted him to go out to al-Rabdhah. And Qatada narrated that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said to Abu Dharr: If you see Madinah's buildings reaching Sala' then leave it, and he pointed to Syria. Then during Uthman's governance its buildings reached Sala', so he left for Syria, and he objected to some things done by Muawiya, so Muawiya complained of him to Uthman. So Uthman wrote to Abu Dharr: Come to us, for we are more mindful of your right and better in companionship than Muawiya. Abu Dharr said: Hearing and obedience. So he came to Uthman, then asked permission to go out to al-Rabdhah, and he permitted him, and he died. And the narration of these two great imams Muhammad ibn Sirin and Qatada, from the Tabi'un and Ahl al-Sunnah, this story is more befitting of Abu Dharr and Uthman than the narration of others from the people of innovation.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a historical defense of Uthman against the accusation that he unjustly banished Abu Dharr al-Ghifari. The author begins by describing the accusation: that Abu Dharr criticized Uthman and his governors for accumulating wealth and building high structures, and that he considered such enjoyment of worldly adornment forbidden. He would enter upon the caliphs and recite the Quranic verse threatening hoarders with branding in Hellfire, and would confront them with harsh speech. Uthman then gave him a choice: either stay and refrain from stirring discord, or go to a place where his words would not be heard and his actions not condemned. The author then comments that if the banishment were proven in this manner, it would be justified, but it is not proven; rather, Abu Dharr himself chose to go to al-Rabdhah. The author then provides a counter-narrative from Ahl al-Sunnah sources: when Abu Dharr came to Syria, he asked Uthman's permission to go to al-Rabdhah, but Uthman offered to keep him with provisions, and Abu Dharr declined, so Uthman permitted him to leave. Another narration from Qatada adds that the Prophet had foretold that when Madinah's buildings reach Sala', Abu Dharr should leave, and that occurred during Uthman's time. Abu Dharr then went to Syria, criticized Muawiya, and Uthman recalled him and then permitted him to go to al-Rabdhah. The author concludes that the narrations of the trustworthy imams from the Tabi'un and Ahl al-Sunnah are more befitting of the character of Abu Dharr and Uthman than the narrations of the people of innovation (i.e., the Rawafid/Shia).

Key Terms
أبو ذر الغفاري
عثمان بن عفان
الربذة
روافض
محمد بن سيرين
قتادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman banished Abu Dharr out of enmity and injustice.
Correction: Baqillani shows that Abu Dharr himself chose to leave, and the narrations of trustworthy scholars present a different sequence of events.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what was the main reason Abu Dharr left for al-Rabdhah?
A) Uthman banished him forcefully
B) He chose to go on his own accord
C) He was sent by the Prophet's command
D) He fled from Muawiya

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends Uthman by presenting alternative narrations that show Abu Dharr's departure was voluntary and amicable, challenging the sectarian narrative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative report about a fellow believer, do you immediately accept it, or do you seek alternative accounts as Baqillani did? How will you train yourself to withhold judgment until you have examined multiple perspectives, especially regarding contentious issues?
?
Abu Dharr's zeal for justice led him to publicly rebuke the caliph, causing discord. Have you ever been so convinced of your own righteousness that you neglected the Prophet's command to be gentle and avoid fitna? In what situation will you commit to choosing wisdom over confrontation, even when you believe you are right?
?
The author argues that the reliable narrations are 'more befitting' of the characters of Abu Dharr and Uthman. Are you quick to assume the worst about people you disagree with, especially about historical figures? How would your heart change if you consistently gave the benefit of the doubt and sought the most charitable interpretation of others' actions?

Refuting the Accusation Against Uthman
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman gave refuge to Al-Hakam, whom the Prophet expelled.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman sheltered Al-Hakam, an alleged outcast of the Prophet.

Core Idea
The accusation against Uthman is based on unreliable reports; the Prophet himself permitted Al-Hakam's return.

This passage is a defense of Uthman ibn Affan against a common polemical accusation. The claim is that Uthman gave refuge to Al-Hakam ibn Abi al-As, whom the Prophet had expelled. Baqillani presents two counter-arguments: first, the story of expulsion is uncertain and second, Uthman had the Prophet's permission. This lesson unpacks his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice Baqillani's direct refutation style.
The passage contains two main arguments.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find where Baqillani first denies the claim outright, then presents an alternative narrative. Then see the second argument about Uthman's request to the Prophet.
The first argument relies on uncertainty; the second on a narrated permission.
3
Evaluate the reasoning
Ask yourself: How does Baqillani dismiss the reasons for Al-Hakam's expulsion? Why does he consider the narration about Uthman's request significant?
He calls the reasons 'nonsense' and uses the narration to show Uthman acted permissibly.
4
Reflect on the ruling principle
Baqillani concludes that a ruler can act on his own knowledge. Consider how this principle defends Uthman's action.
This is a fiqhi principle relevant to the case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بأنه آوى الحكم طريد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه باطل لأن أكثر الناس ينكره ويقول إن الحكم خرج بأمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنه كف وكبر فاستأذن في الخروج إلى أهله فأذن له وعلى أن القوم لا يدرون ما سبب طرده فمنهم من يقول إنه كان يحاكي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مشيته ومنهم من يذكر أنه كان يحاكيه خلف الصفوف وكل هذا من الترهات. وقد روي عن غير طريق أيضاً أن عثمان كان قد قال لأبي بكر وعمر: إني كنت استأذنت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رده فأذن في ذلك فطالباه بآخر معه يشهد بذلك فلم يجد فلما ولى عمل على أمره رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وليس هذا الحكم مما لا يجوز عمل الحاكم فيه وحكمه بعلمه فلا متعلق فيما ذكروه من ذلك.
And as for their claim that he gave refuge to Al-Hakam, the outcast of the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, it is false, because most people deny it and say that Al-Hakam left by the command of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, because he had become blind and old, so he asked permission to go out to his family and he permitted him. And also, the people do not know the reason for his expulsion; some say that he used to imitate the Prophet's walk, and some mention that he used to imitate him behind the rows, and all of this is nonsense. And it has also been narrated through another chain that Uthman had said to Abu Bakr and Umar: I asked the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, to allow him to return, and he permitted that. So they demanded another person with him to witness that, but he did not find one. When he assumed authority, he acted upon the matter of the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him. And this judgement is not something in which the ruler cannot act upon his own knowledge, so there is no basis in what they mentioned.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage refutes the accusation that Uthman gave refuge to Al-Hakam, whom the Prophet had expelled. The author first declares the claim false. He then gives two counter-arguments: first, most people deny the story and instead say that Al-Hakam left Medina with the Prophet's permission due to old age and blindness. The reason for his expulsion is uncertain and the various explanations (imitating the Prophet's walk) are dismissed as nonsense. Second, there is a narration that Uthman himself had asked the Prophet to allow Al-Hakam to return, and the Prophet permitted it, though Uthman could not produce a witness. Later, when Uthman became caliph, he acted on what the Prophet had allowed. The author concludes that there is no prohibition for a ruler to act on his own knowledge, so the accusation has no basis.

Key Terms
الحكم
طريد رسول الله
عثمان
أبو بكر
عمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman sheltered someone the Prophet expelled, making him guilty of disobeying the Prophet.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Prophet had permitted Al-Hakam's return, and Uthman acted on that permission. The claim of expulsion is unreliable.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say about the reason for Al-Hakam's expulsion?
A) He was expelled for apostasy
B) The reason is unknown and various claims are nonsense
C) He was expelled for stealing
D) He was expelled because he imitated the Prophet's speech

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends Uthman by showing the accusation is based on uncertain reports and that Uthman had the Prophet's permission to allow Al-Hakam's return.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a story about someone's wrongdoing without verifying its source? This lesson shows Baqillani's method: dismiss vague reports and rely on confirmed testimony. What reputation have you damaged by passing along unverified news? Will you now seek out the truth before speaking, especially about fellow Muslims?
?
Baqillani argues that a ruler can act on his own certain knowledge, even without witnesses. Is there an area of your faith—like a prayer, a ruling, or a conviction—where you know the truth but hesitate because you fear others' doubts? What one step will you take today to act on that certain knowledge, trusting that Allah knows your sincerity?
?
The Prophet allowed al-Hakam to return, and ʿUthmān implemented that permission despite criticism. Do you have the courage to follow the Prophet's guidance even when it is unpopular or misunderstood by others? What social pressure is holding you back from obeying a clear command? Resolve now to obey over seeking approval.

Ali's Appointment to Recite Surah Bara'ah
The author cites the Prophet sending Ali to recite Bara'ah, demonstrating Ali's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's appointment of Ali to recite Surah Bara'ah demonstrates Ali's special status and suitability for conveying divine messages.

Core Idea
Only a man from the Prophet's family could convey this critical message.

This passage uses two key evidences—the analogy with Moses and Aaron, and the Prophet's explicit statement—to establish Ali's unique qualification. The author highlights the challenging nature of the task and the high caliber of the audience to underscore Ali's worth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the argument without imposing any interpretation yet.
2
Notice the analogy with Moses and Aaron
The author begins by comparing the Prophet's appointment of Ali to Moses appointing Aaron without hatred. This shows that such appointments are not due to personal dislike.
3
Understand the Prophet's statement
The Prophet said 'None should convey on my behalf except a man from me.' This limits the role to a relative, indicating Ali's special family tie.
4
Consider the difficulty of the task
Sending Ali to recite Bara'ah to the Quraysh, described as contentious and intelligent, shows that only someone of high worth could handle it.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
The passage builds a cumulative case: analogy, explicit statement, and the difficulty of the mission all point to Ali's excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استخلف موسى أخاه هارون لما توجه لكلام ربه من غير بغض ولا قلى وقوله : «لا يُؤدِّي عني إلا رجل مني»، وإنفاذه بسورة براءة يقرؤها على المشركين بمكة؛ وهذا أمر لا يليه إلا أهل القَدْرِ والنباهة ومن يصلح للتحمل والأداء عن رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم إلى مثل قريش مع وفارة عقولهم وصحة أحلامهم وما وصفهم الله به فقال: بل هم قوم خصمون.
Moses appointed his brother Aaron when he went to the speech of his Lord without hatred or rancor. And his (the Prophet's) statement: 'None should convey on my behalf except a man from me.' And his sending (Ali) with Surah Bara'ah to recite it to the polytheists in Mecca. This is a matter that only people of worth and sagacity undertake, and those who are fit to bear and convey from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, to the likes of Quraysh, with the abundance of their intellects, soundness of their forbearance, and what Allah described them with when He said: 'Nay, they are a contentious people.'
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of Ali's high status by citing the Prophet's action and statement. The author begins by drawing an analogy: just as Moses appointed Aaron without rancor, the Prophet appointed Ali to convey a critical message. The Prophet explicitly said 'None should convey on my behalf except a man from me'—meaning a relative from his clan. Then the author mentions that the Prophet sent Ali to recite Surah Bara'ah to the Quraysh, a task requiring great courage and eloquence. The author emphasizes that this task is only given to those of high worth and suitability, especially given the sharp intellect and contentious nature of the Quraysh, as Allah described them. Thus, the selection of Ali proves his excellence.

Key Terms
يؤدي عني
براءة
خصمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'man from me' is often misunderstood as any Muslim.
Correction: Context shows it refers to a relative from the Prophet's clan, specifically Ali.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why was Ali chosen to recite Surah Bara'ah to the Quraysh?
A) Because he was the best reciter
B) Because he was a man from the Prophet's family
C) Because he was older than others
D) Because he was brave

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's appointment of Ali to recite Bara'ah proves his high rank and fitness for conveying divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Prophet entrusted Ali with a mission that required great courage and intellect, he did not hesitate. Is there a responsibility in your life that you have been avoiding because it seems too difficult? What would it take for you to step forward like Ali?
?
The author notes that Quraysh were 'a contentious people,' yet Ali was chosen to face them. Whom do you find difficult to speak the truth to? How can you prepare yourself to convey Allah's message to them, trusting in His support?
?
The Prophet said, 'None should convey on my behalf except a man from me.' This implies that conveying the truth requires a deep personal connection to the one who sent you. How deep is your connection to the Prophet? What will you do today to strengthen that bond?

Hadith of Fatima: Allah Chose Two Men
The Prophet consoles Fatima by saying Allah chose her father and husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Prophet's consolation to Fatima and the high status of Ali implied by this hadith.

Core Idea
Allah deliberately chose Fatima's father and husband from all humanity.

This hadith is a beautiful example of the Prophet's tenderness towards his daughter and his way of elevating her spirits. More importantly, it serves as a clear indication of Ali's lofty rank, as Allah specially selected him along with the Prophet Himself. Let's examine the wording and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the Prophet's words and the comfort offered to Fatima.
Notice the phrase 'اطلع على أهل الأرض فاختار منهم رجلين'.
2
Understand the context
Fatima complained about some worldly difficulty; the Prophet responded with this statement to console her.
This shows the Prophet's compassion and wisdom.
3
Identify the key claim
Allah looked at all the people of the earth and chose two men: one is Fatima's father (Muhammad) and the other is her husband (Ali).
4
Reflect on the significance
This hadith directly elevates Ali's status, placing him as chosen by Allah alongside the Prophet.
It is a virtue of Ali, not a claim of equality.
5
Address a common misunderstanding
Some may think this implies Ali is equal to the Prophet, but it shows his high rank, not equality in prophethood.
Prophethood is unique to Muhammad; Ali is a companion and the Prophet's son-in-law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فضائله قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لفاطمة، وقد شكت له بعض حالها: «أما ترضين أن الله قد اطلع على أهل الأرض فاختار منهم رجلين جعل أحدهم أباك وجعل الآخر بعلك؟»
And among his virtues is his saying, peace be upon him, to Fatima when she complained to him about some of her situation: 'Are you not content that Allah looked upon the people of the earth and chose from them two men, making one of them your father and the other your husband?'
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage presents another virtue of Ali by quoting a hadith of the Prophet to his daughter Fatima. When Fatima complained, the Prophet consoled her by telling her that Allah deliberately chose two men from all humanity: her father (the Prophet himself) and her husband (Ali). This hadith directly elevates Ali to a status second only to the Prophet, as being chosen by Allah along with the Prophet.

Key Terms
اطلع
اختار
رجلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith implies Ali is equal to the Prophet.
Correction: The hadith shows Ali's high rank, but not equality with prophethood.

Checkpoint
Who are the two men chosen by Allah according to the hadith?
A) Abu Bakr and Umar
B) Muhammad and Ali
C) Muhammad and Fatima
D) Ali and Hasan

Key Takeaway
The Prophet assured Fatima that her father and husband were the two men specially chosen by Allah from all humanity, affirming Ali’s unparalleled honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Fatima complained about hardship, but the Prophet redirected her to an immense spiritual blessing. When you are dissatisfied with your worldly circumstances, do you stop to count the unique blessings Allah has chosen specifically for you—people, relationships, or roles? Will you today consciously thank Allah for those He has placed in your life, especially those who guide you to Him?
?
Allah looked at everyone on earth and singled out two men for Fatima. Do you believe that Allah has specifically chosen the people around you for a purpose? Are you treating your father, spouse, or spiritual mentors as divinely selected gifts, or do you take them for granted?
?
This hadith reveals that the Prophet's comfort for Fatima was not material but spiritual—reminding her of her honored position. When you face trials, do you seek comfort in your status before Allah (being chosen through faith) or only in fixing the worldly problem? What would change if you truly felt 'chosen' by Allah?

Hadith of the Bird: Ali as the Most Beloved
al-Baqillani cites the hadith of the bird as a miracle showing Ali's virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the hadith of the bird as a miracle and an indication of Ali's high status.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer was instantly answered, revealing Ali as the most beloved to Allah.

This hadith is a well-known episode from the Prophet's life, often cited in discussions of virtues (fadail) of the Companions. The passage from al-Baqillani presents it as a clear sign of Ali's elevated rank, as the Prophet's supplication was immediately fulfilled. Let us examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Familiarise yourself with the wording.
2
Understand the context
The Prophet had received a roasted bird as a gift. He then made a specific supplication.
This context helps appreciate the miracle.
3
Examine the supplication
Note that the Prophet asked for 'the most beloved of creation to You' — a request that directly seeks divine favour.
The phrase 'أحب الخلق إليك' is key.
4
Observe the outcome
Ali came immediately and ate with the Prophet. This instant answer shows Ali is that beloved one.
5
Reflect on theological significance
This event serves as a miracle (karama) for Ali and evidence of his virtue. It also shows the power of the Prophet's prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله صلّى الله عليه وسلم: «اللهم انتني بأحب الخلق إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطائر»، فجاء علي فأكل معه من الطائر المشوي الذي كان أهْدِي إليه.
And his saying, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, bring to me the most beloved of creation to You to eat with me from this bird,' so Ali came and ate with him from the roasted bird that had been gifted to him.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage cites a famous hadith in which the Prophet asked Allah to bring the most beloved creature to share a meal of roasted bird. Immediately, Ali arrived and ate with him. This serves as a sign that Ali is the most beloved to Allah among all creation, as the prayer was answered instantly.

Key Terms
أحب الخلق
الطائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith implies Ali is superior to all other Companions in every respect.
Correction: The hadith indicates Ali's high status in this specific incident, but other virtues are attributed to other Companions in other hadith.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet ask Allah for before Ali arrived?
A) To send someone to help him
B) To bring the most beloved creation to eat with him
C) To bring a bird from paradise
D) To test Ali's loyalty

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the bird exemplifies how the Prophet's prayers were answered instantly, affirming Ali as one of the most beloved to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were among the Companions and heard the Prophet make this supplication, would you have hoped earnestly that it was you? Why? What does your answer reveal about your love for Allah?
?
The Prophet's prayer was answered instantly. How does this challenge your own level of certainty that Allah hears and answers your prayers? What is one prayer you have been hesitant to make with full conviction?
?
Ali was chosen because of his love for Allah. Look at your own life: what evidence exists that you are among those most beloved to Allah? If there is little, what will you change starting today?

Umar's Acknowledgment of Ali's Knowledge
The author cites Umar's famous statement acknowledging Ali's indispensable knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Baqillani cites Umar's famous statement as evidence for Ali's authority in legal matters.

Core Idea
Umar's admission shows Ali's indispensability in Islamic jurisprudence.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani presents a powerful testimony from Umar ibn al-Khattab, the second caliph. Umar's statement 'Were it not for Ali, Umar would have perished' is not a casual remark but a recognition of Ali's superior knowledge in resolving complex legal issues. The author uses this to underscore the Companions' consensus on Ali's virtue and expertise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first mentions the general consensus of the Companions before quoting Umar's specific statement.
Pay attention to the key terms: إعظام, لولا علي لهلك عمر, مطابقتهم.
2
Analyze Umar's statement
Reflect on the meaning of 'Lola Ali lahalaka Umar.' Why would a caliph like Umar say this? What does it imply about Ali's role in legal rulings?
Consider that Umar was known for his own knowledge, so this admission is significant.
3
Connect to the author's argument
Understand how this quote fits into Baqillani's larger discussion about Ali's status. The author uses this as proof of Ali's pre-eminence and the Companions' consensus on his knowledge.
This passage is part of a broader defense of Ali's virtues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا مع ما ظهر من إعظام كافة الصحابة له وإطباقهم على علمه وفضله وثاقب فهمه ورأيه وفقه نفسه وقول مِثْل عمر فيه : لولا عليّ لهلك عمر وكثرة مطابقتهم له في الأحكام وسماع قوله في الحلال والحرام.
This is with what appeared of the veneration of all the Companions for him, and their consensus on his knowledge, virtue, penetrating understanding, opinion, and jurisprudence of himself, and the statement of the like of Umar concerning him: 'Were it not for Ali, Umar would have perished,' and their frequent agreement with him in rulings and listening to his word concerning the lawful and unlawful.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage highlights the consensus of the Companions on Ali's authority. It first states that all Companions venerated him and agreed on his knowledge and insight. Then it specifically quotes Umar, the second caliph, saying 'Lola Ali lahalaka Umar'—an admission that without Ali's guidance, Umar would have been ruined in legal matters. The passage also notes that the Companions frequently conformed to Ali's rulings and listened to his judgments on halal and haram, further confirming his pre-eminence.

Key Terms
إعظام
لولا علي لهلك عمر
مطابقتهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar's statement implies Ali was more knowledgeable than Umar in all respects.
Correction: The passage shows this statement is specific to certain legal issues where Ali's insight was crucial. It does not claim Ali was superior in all fields, but highlights his indispensable role in jurisprudence.

Checkpoint
What did Umar say about Ali according to the passage?
A) Ali is the best of the Companions
B) Were it not for Ali, Umar would have perished
C) Ali is the rightful caliph
D) Ali is the most learned in Quran

Key Takeaway
Umar's statement is a key proof of Ali's authority in Islamic jurisprudence, endorsed by the consensus of the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you admitted that someone else's knowledge was essential for your own understanding in a matter of faith? Is there an area of your life where pride prevents you from saying 'Were it not for that person, I would be lost'?
?
Umar, the second caliph, openly acknowledged Ali's expertise despite his own authority. In your own relationships—with family, colleagues, or teachers—do you freely recognize the strengths of others, or do you feel threatened? What would change in your interactions if you embraced Umar's humility?
?
This lesson shows that even the most knowledgeable Companions relied on Ali for guidance on the lawful and unlawful. Who are the people in your life that you rely on for sincere religious guidance? Have you sought them out, or do you rely solely on your own reading? What step will you take this week to seek counsel from someone more knowledgeable?
